Title: Elections Act 2022
Date: 2024-07-01
Publisher: Statute Law Database
Identifier: http://www.legislation.gov.uk/ukpga/2022/37

## Elections Act 2022

                                                   B e it enacted  by the
Queen’s most Excellent Majesty, by and with the advice and consent of the
Lords Spiritual and Temporal, and Commons, in this present Parliament
assembled, and by the authority of the same, as follows:—

### Administration and conduct of elections

#### Voter identification, applications for postal and proxy votes, etc

##### Voter identification

1

Schedule 1  makes provision, including provision amending RPA 1983, in
connection with the production of identification at polling stations by
voters.

##### Power to make regulations about registration, absent voting and other matters

2

Schedule 2 contains provision, including provision amending Schedule 2 to RPA
1983, in connection with applications relating to registration, applications
to vote by post or proxy, and applications for particular kinds of document.

#### Postal and proxy voting

##### Restriction of period for which person can apply for postal vote

3

Schedule 3  contains provision limiting the period for which a person can
apply to vote by post—

3.a

at parliamentary elections in England and Wales and Scotland, and

3.b

at local government elections in England.

##### Handling of postal voting documents by political campaigners

4

4.1

RPA 1983 is amended as follows.

4.2

After section 112 insert—

########### Handling of postal voting documents by political campaigners

4.2.112A

4.2.112A.1

A person who is a political campaigner in respect of a relevant election
commits an offence if the person handles a postal voting document that has
been issued to another person for use in that election.

4.2.112A.2

But a person who handles a postal voting document for use in a relevant
election does not commit the offence if—

4.2.112A.2.a

the person is responsible for, or assists with, the conduct of that election
(for example as a returning officer or a person working under the direction of
a returning officer),

4.2.112A.2.b

the person is engaged in the business of a postal operator, or

4.2.112A.2.c

the person is employed or engaged in a role the duties of which include the
handling of postal packets on behalf of members of an organisation or the
occupants of a communal building,

and the handling is consistent with the person’s duties in that capacity.

4.2.112A.3

Nor does a person commit the offence if the person—

4.2.112A.3.a

is the other person’s spouse, civil partner, parent, grandparent, brother,
sister, child or grandchild, or

4.2.112A.3.b

provides regular care for, or is employed or engaged by an organisation which
provides care for, the other person.

4.2.112A.4

It is a defence for a person charged with the offence to show that the person
did not dishonestly handle the postal voting document for the purpose of
promoting a particular outcome at a relevant election.

4.2.112A.5

Where sufficient evidence is adduced to raise an issue with respect to the
defence under  subsection (4) , the court must assume that the defence is
satisfied unless the prosecution proves beyond reasonable doubt that it is
not.

4.2.112A.6

A person is guilty of a corrupt practice if the person—

4.2.112A.6.a

commits the offence under subsection  (1) , or

4.2.112A.6.b

aids, abets, counsels or procures the commission of that offence.

4.2.112A.7

For the purposes of this section a person is a political campaigner in respect
of a relevant election if any of the following paragraphs applies—

4.2.112A.7.a

the person is a candidate at the election;

4.2.112A.7.b

the person is an election agent of a candidate at the election;

4.2.112A.7.c

the person is a sub-agent of a person within paragraph  (b) ;

4.2.112A.7.d

the person is employed or engaged by a person who is a candidate at the
election for the purposes of that person’s activities as a candidate;

4.2.112A.7.e

the person is a member of a registered political party and carries on an
activity designed to promote a particular outcome at the election;

4.2.112A.7.f

the person is employed or engaged by a registered political party in
connection with the party’s political activities;

4.2.112A.7.g

the person is employed or engaged by a person within any of paragraphs  (a)
to  (f)  to carry on an activity designed to promote a particular outcome at
the election;

4.2.112A.7.h

the person is employed or engaged by a person within  paragraph (g)  to carry
on an activity designed to promote a particular outcome at the election.

4.2.112A.8

In this section—

            “ postal operator ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 of the
Postal Services Act 2011 (see section 27(3) to (5) of that Act);
“ postal voting document ” means a postal ballot paper, postal voting
statement, declaration of identity or envelope that has been issued to a
person for the purpose of enabling the person to vote by post at a relevant
election;
“ relevant election ” means—
a parliamentary election, or
a local government election in England.

4.2.112A.9

For the purposes of this section, an envelope—

4.2.112A.9.a

that is not a postal voting document, but

4.2.112A.9.b

that contains a postal ballot paper, postal voting statement or declaration of
identity that has been issued to a person for the purpose of enabling the
person to vote by post at a relevant election,

is to be treated as if it were a postal voting document that has been issued
to the person for use in the election.

4.2.112A.10

In this section, any reference to a person who is “engaged” by another person,
or to a person who provides care for another person, includes a reference to a
person who is engaged or provides care otherwise than for payment or promise
of payment.

4.2.112A.11

For the purposes of  subsection (3) (a) , two people living together as if
they were a married couple or civil partners are treated as if they were
spouses or civil partners of each other.

4.3

In section 160 (persons reported personally guilty of corrupt or illegal
practices), in subsection (4A) for “or 62B” substitute  “, 62B or 112A” .

4.4

In section 168 (prosecutions for corrupt practices), in subsection (1)(a)(i),
before “above” insert  “or 112A” .

4.5

In section 173 (incapacities on conviction of corrupt or illegal practice), in
subsection (2)  for “or 62B” substitute  “, 62B or 112A” .

##### Handing in postal voting documents

5

5.1

RPA 1983 is amended as follows.

5.2

Schedule 1 (Parliamentary elections rules) is amended in accordance with
subsections (3) and (4).

5.3

In rule 32 (admission to polling station), in paragraph (1), after sub-
paragraph (b) insert—

5.3.ba

where regulations under rule 45(1B)(a) or (b) provide that a postal ballot
paper or postal voting statement may be returned by hand to a polling station,
persons aged 18 or over returning such a document by hand;

.

5.4

In rule 45 (the count)—

5.4.a

in paragraph (1B)—

5.4.a.i

omit “and” at the end of sub-paragraph (c);

5.4.a.ii

insert  “and”  at the end of sub-paragraph (d);

5.4.a.iii

after sub-paragraph (d) insert—

5.4.a.iii.e

where regulations contain provision made by virtue of paragraph 12ZA of
Schedule 2 (handing in postal voting documents), the postal ballot paper is
not one that falls to be rejected in accordance with that provision.

;

5.4.b

in paragraph (2)—

5.4.b.i

for sub-paragraph (a) substitute—

5.4.b.i.a

it is returned in the prescribed manner, accompanied by the declaration of
identity duly signed and authenticated, and reaches the returning officer
before the close of the poll,

;

5.4.b.ii

insert  “and”  at the end of sub-paragraph (b);

5.4.b.iii

after sub-paragraph (b) insert—

5.4.b.iii.c

where regulations contain provision made by virtue of paragraph 12ZB of
Schedule 2 (handing in postal voting documents: Northern Ireland), the postal
ballot paper is not one that falls to be rejected in accordance with that
provision.

5.5

In Schedule 2 (provisions which may be contained in regulations as to
registration etc), after paragraph 12 insert—

5.5.12ZA

5.5.12ZA.1

Where regulations under rule 45(1B)(a) or (b) in Schedule 1 provide that a
postal voting document may be returned by hand to a polling station or to the
returning officer, provision within this paragraph.

5.5.12ZA.2

Provision—

5.5.12ZA.2.a

requiring a person who seeks to hand in a postal voting document to complete a
form containing prescribed information,

5.5.12ZA.2.b

requiring a relevant officer to reject a postal voting document handed in by a
person who fails to provide all the prescribed information on such a form, and

5.5.12ZA.2.c

about the arrangements to be made in respect of such forms.

5.5.12ZA.3

Provision requiring a relevant officer—

5.5.12ZA.3.a

to reject all postal voting documents handed in together by a person where the
relevant officer has reasonable cause to suspect that the documents are handed
in on behalf of more than the prescribed number of electors;

5.5.12ZA.3.b

to reject a postal voting document handed in by a person, or all postal voting
documents handed in together by a person, on a particular occasion, where the
relevant officer has reasonable cause to suspect that, taking that document or
those documents together with any postal voting documents handed in by the
person on any previous occasion (disregarding any that were rejected), the
person has handed in postal voting documents on behalf of more than the
prescribed number of electors.

5.5.12ZA.4

In  sub-paragraph (3) —

5.5.12ZA.4.a

references to postal voting documents handed in by a person are to postal
voting documents—

5.5.12ZA.4.a.i

all relating to the same election, or

5.5.12ZA.4.a.ii

where more than one poll is to be taken on a day, each of which relates to an
election the poll at which is to be taken on that day,

but do not include references to a postal voting document issued to that
person;

5.5.12ZA.4.b

“ electors ” means persons who are electors in relation to an election to
which any of the postal voting documents handed in by the person relates.

5.5.12ZA.5

Provision authorising a relevant officer to reject a postal voting document
handed in by a person where the relevant officer knows or has reasonable cause
to suspect that, in handing in the document, the person commits an offence
under section 112A (offences relating to handling of postal voting documents).

5.5.12ZA.6

Provision as to the arrangements to be made in respect of the documents
mentioned in  sub-paragraph (7) , including provision about—

5.5.12ZA.6.a

the procedure to be followed in respect of those documents;

5.5.12ZA.6.b

storage of those documents;

5.5.12ZA.6.c

disposal of those documents;

5.5.12ZA.6.d

transfer of those documents to—

5.5.12ZA.6.d.i

the returning officer;

5.5.12ZA.6.d.ii

the registration officer.

5.5.12ZA.7

The documents are—

5.5.12ZA.7.a

a postal voting document that is rejected;

5.5.12ZA.7.b

a postal voting document that—

5.5.12ZA.7.b.i

is brought into a polling station or into the offices of the returning officer
so that it may be handed in to a person, but

5.5.12ZA.7.b.ii

is left behind there (without being handed in).

5.5.12ZA.8

Provision requiring prescribed information about postal voting documents that
are handed in, or about the documents mentioned in  sub-paragraph (7) , to be
supplied to—

5.5.12ZA.8.a

the returning officer;

5.5.12ZA.8.b

the registration officer.

5.5.12ZA.9

Provision about the notification of the persons mentioned in  sub-paragraph
(10)  where a postal ballot paper is—

5.5.12ZA.9.a

rejected, or

5.5.12ZA.9.b

left behind as mentioned in  sub-paragraph (7) (b) .

5.5.12ZA.10

The persons are—

5.5.12ZA.10.a

the person whose ballot paper it is;

5.5.12ZA.10.b

where that person is a proxy—

5.5.12ZA.10.b.i

that person, and

5.5.12ZA.10.b.ii

the elector for whom the person voted as proxy on that paper.

5.5.12ZA.11

Provision as to the meaning of any reference in the regulations to—

5.5.12ZA.11.a

a person seeking to hand in a postal voting document;

5.5.12ZA.11.b

a postal voting document being handed in.

5.5.12ZA.12

In this paragraph—

   “ postal voting document ” means a postal ballot paper, postal voting
statement or other document that has been issued to a person for the purpose
of enabling the person to vote by post at a relevant election;
“ rejected ” means rejected in accordance with regulations made by virtue of
this paragraph;
“ relevant election ” means—
a parliamentary election in England and Wales or Scotland, or
a local government election in England;
“ relevant officer ” means—
where a postal voting document is handed in at a polling station—
the person presiding at the polling station, or
a clerk at the polling station;
where a postal voting document is handed in to the returning officer—
that officer, or
a person acting under the authority of that officer.

5.5.12ZB

5.5.12ZB.1

Where regulations under rule 45(2)(a) in Schedule 1 provide that a postal
voting document may be returned by hand to the returning officer, provision
within this paragraph.

5.5.12ZB.2

Provision—

5.5.12ZB.2.a

requiring a person who seeks to hand in a postal voting document to complete a
form containing prescribed information,

5.5.12ZB.2.b

requiring the returning officer to reject a postal voting document handed in
by a person who fails to provide all the prescribed information on such a
form, and

5.5.12ZB.2.c

about the arrangements to be made in respect of such forms.

5.5.12ZB.3

Provision requiring the returning officer—

5.5.12ZB.3.a

to reject all postal voting documents handed in together by a person where the
returning officer has reasonable cause to suspect that the documents are
handed in on behalf of more than the prescribed number of electors;

5.5.12ZB.3.b

to reject a postal voting document handed in by a person, or all postal voting
documents handed in together by a person, on a particular occasion, where the
returning officer has reasonable cause to suspect that, taking that document
or those documents together with any postal voting documents handed in by the
person on any previous occasion (disregarding any that were rejected), the
person has handed in postal voting documents on behalf of more than the
prescribed number of electors.

5.5.12ZB.4

In  sub-paragraph (3) —

5.5.12ZB.4.a

references to postal voting documents handed in by a person are to postal
voting documents all relating to the same election, but do not include
references to a postal voting document issued to that person;

5.5.12ZB.4.b

“ electors ” means persons who are electors in relation to the election to
which the postal voting documents handed in by the person relate.

5.5.12ZB.5

Provision authorising the returning officer to reject a postal voting document
handed in by a person where the returning officer knows or has reasonable
cause to suspect that, in handing in the document, the person commits an
offence under section 112A (offences relating to handling of postal voting
documents).

5.5.12ZB.6

Provision as to the arrangements to be made in respect of the documents
mentioned in  sub-paragraph (7) , including provision about—

5.5.12ZB.6.a

the procedure to be followed in respect of those documents;

5.5.12ZB.6.b

storage of those documents;

5.5.12ZB.6.c

disposal of those documents.

5.5.12ZB.7

The documents are—

5.5.12ZB.7.a

a postal voting document that is rejected;

5.5.12ZB.7.b

a postal voting document that—

5.5.12ZB.7.b.i

is brought into the offices of the returning officer so that it may be handed
in to a person, but

5.5.12ZB.7.b.ii

is left behind there (without being handed in).

5.5.12ZB.8

Provision about the notification of the persons mentioned in  sub-paragraph
(9)  where a postal ballot paper is—

5.5.12ZB.8.a

rejected, or

5.5.12ZB.8.b

left behind as mentioned in  sub-paragraph (7) (b) .

5.5.12ZB.9

The persons are—

5.5.12ZB.9.a

the person whose ballot paper it is;

5.5.12ZB.9.b

where that person is a proxy—

5.5.12ZB.9.b.i

that person, and

5.5.12ZB.9.b.ii

the elector for whom the person voted as proxy on that paper.

5.5.12ZB.10

Provision as to the meaning of any reference in the regulations to—

5.5.12ZB.10.a

a person seeking to hand in a postal voting document;

5.5.12ZB.10.b

a postal voting document being handed in.

5.5.12ZB.11

In this paragraph—

   “ postal voting document ” means a postal ballot paper, declaration of
identity, or other document that has been issued to a person for the purpose
of enabling the person to vote by post at a parliamentary election in Northern
Ireland;
“ rejected ” means rejected in accordance with regulations made by virtue of
this paragraph.

##### Limit on number of electors for whom a proxy can vote

6

Schedule 4 —

6.a

contains amendments limiting a person’s entitlement to vote as proxy—

6.a.i

at parliamentary elections, and

6.a.ii

at local government elections in England,

(see paragraphs  6 (4)  and  7 (2) ), and

6.b

makes related provision about proxy voting and proxy appointments.

##### Requirement of secrecy

7

7.1

Section 66 of RPA 1983 (requirement of secrecy) is amended as follows.

7.2

After subsection (3) insert—

7.2.3A

No person may—

7.2.3A.a

except for some purpose authorised by law, obtain or attempt to obtain
information, or communicate at any time to any other person any information,
as to the number or other unique identifying mark on the back of a ballot
paper sent to a person for voting by post at a relevant election;

7.2.3A.b

except for some purpose authorised by law, obtain or attempt to obtain
information, or communicate at any time to any other person any information,
as to the official mark on a ballot paper sent to a person for voting by post
at a relevant election;

7.2.3A.c

obtain or attempt to obtain information, in the circumstances mentioned in
subsection  (3B) , as to the candidate for whom a person voting by post at a
relevant election (“ V ”) is about to vote or has voted;

7.2.3A.d

communicate at any time to any other person information obtained in
contravention of paragraph  (c) .

7.2.3B

The circumstances referred to in subsection  (3A) (c)  are where V is about to
mark, is in the process of marking, or has just marked, a ballot paper sent to
V for voting by post at the election.

7.2.3C

But—

7.2.3C.a

a person (“ E ”) who is voting by proxy does not contravene subsection  (3A)
by obtaining or attempting to obtain from the person appointed as E’s proxy
information as to a matter mentioned in paragraph  (a)  or  (c)  of that
subsection that relates to E’s vote, and

7.2.3C.b

a person who is appointed as proxy for an elector does not contravene
subsection  (3A)  by communicating to that elector information as to a matter
mentioned in paragraph  (a)  or  (c)  of that subsection that relates to that
elector’s vote.

7.2.3D

Subsection  (3A) (c)  and  (d)  does not apply where the purpose (or main
purpose) for which the information is sought or communicated is its use for
the purposes of—

7.2.3D.a

a published statement relating to the way in which voters intend to vote or
have voted at the relevant election, or

7.2.3D.b

a published forecast as to the result of that election which is based on
information given by voters.

7.2.3E

In subsection  (3D) —

7.2.3E.a

“ forecast ” includes estimate;

7.2.3E.b

“ published ” means made available to the public at large or to any section of
the public, in whatever form and by whatever means;

7.2.3E.c

the reference to the result of the relevant election is a reference to the
result of the election either as a whole or so far as any particular candidate
or candidates at the election is or are concerned.

7.2.3F

A person voting as proxy for an elector at a relevant election—

7.2.3F.a

must not communicate at any time to any person other than that elector any
information as to the candidate for whom the person is about to vote, or has
voted, as proxy for that elector;

7.2.3F.b

except for some purpose authorised by law, must not communicate at any time to
any person other than that elector the number or other unique identifying mark
on the back of a ballot paper sent or delivered to the person for voting as
proxy for that elector.

7.3

After subsection (4) insert—

7.3.4A

No person having undertaken to assist a relevant voter to vote at a relevant
election may communicate at any time to any person except that voter any
information as to—

7.3.4A.a

the candidate for whom the voter intends to vote or has voted, or

7.3.4A.b

the number or other unique identifying mark on the back of the ballot paper
given for the use of the voter.

7.3.4B

In  subsection (4A)  “ relevant voter ” means a voter who is blind, has
another disability, or is unable to read.

7.4

In  subsection (5) , after “to vote”, in the first place it occurs, insert
“at an election in Scotland or Wales under the local government Act” .

7.5

After subsection (6) insert—

7.5.6A

In this section, “ relevant election ” means—

7.5.6A.a

a parliamentary election, or

7.5.6A.b

an election in England under the local government Act.

7.6

In rule 31 of Schedule 1 to RPA 1983 (Parliamentary elections rules:
notification of requirement of secrecy)—

7.6.a

in paragraph (1)(a), for “blind voter” substitute  “relevant voter” ;

7.6.b

after paragraph (1) insert—

7.6.b.1A

In paragraph (1)(a) “ relevant voter ” means a voter who is blind, has another
disability, or is unable to read.

#### Undue influence

##### Undue influence

8

8.1

After section 114 of RPA 1983 insert—

########### Undue influence

8.1.114A

8.1.114A.1

A person is guilty of a corrupt practice if the person is guilty of undue
influence.

8.1.114A.2

A person (“ P ”) is guilty of undue influence if P carries out an activity
falling within subsection  (4)  for the purpose of—

8.1.114A.2.a

inducing or compelling a person to vote in a particular way or to refrain from
voting, or

8.1.114A.2.b

otherwise impeding or preventing the free exercise of the franchise of an
elector or of a proxy for an elector.

8.1.114A.3

A person (“ P ”) is also guilty of undue influence if P carries out an
activity falling within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (f)  of subsection  (4)
on account of—

8.1.114A.3.a

a person having voted in a particular way or refrained from voting, or

8.1.114A.3.b

P assuming a person to have voted in a particular way or to have refrained
from voting.

8.1.114A.4

The following activities fall within this subsection—

8.1.114A.4.a

using or threatening to use violence against a person;

8.1.114A.4.b

damaging or destroying, or threatening to damage or destroy, a person’s
property;

8.1.114A.4.c

damaging or threatening to damage a person’s reputation;

8.1.114A.4.d

causing or threatening to cause financial loss to a person;

8.1.114A.4.e

causing spiritual injury to, or placing undue spiritual pressure on, a person;

8.1.114A.4.f

doing any other act designed to intimidate a person;

8.1.114A.4.g

doing any act designed to deceive a person in relation to the administration
of an election.

8.1.114A.5

For the purposes of subsections  (2)  and  (3)  an activity is carried out by
a person (“ P ”) if it is carried out—

8.1.114A.5.a

by P,

8.1.114A.5.b

by P jointly with one or more other persons, or

8.1.114A.5.c

by one or more other persons on behalf of P and with P’s authority or consent.

8.1.114A.6

In subsection  (4) (f)  and  (g)  “ act ” includes an omission (and references
to the doing of an act are to be read accordingly).

8.1.114A.7

This section does not have effect in relation to an election in Scotland or
Wales under the local government Act.

8.2

In section 115 of RPA 1983 (undue influence)—

8.2.a

in subsection (1), after “influence” insert  “in relation to an election in
Scotland or Wales under the local government Act” ;

8.2.b

in subsection (2), after “influence” insert  “in relation to an election in
Scotland or Wales under the local government Act” ;

8.2.c

in the heading, after “influence” insert  “: local government elections in
Scotland and Wales” .

8.3

Schedule 5  contains further provision relating to this section.

#### Assistance with voting for persons with disabilities

##### Assistance with voting for persons with disabilities

9

9.1

Schedule 1 to RPA 1983 (Parliamentary elections rules) is amended as follows.

9.2

In rule 29 (equipment of polling stations)—

9.2.a

in paragraph (3A), for sub-paragraph (b) substitute—

9.2.a.b

such equipment as it is reasonable to provide for the purposes of enabling, or
making it easier for, relevant persons to vote independently in the manner
directed by rule 37 (including in relation to voting secretly).

;

9.2.b

after paragraph (3A) insert—

9.2.b.3B

In this rule, “ relevant persons ” means persons who find it difficult or
impossible to vote in the manner directed by rule 37 because of—

9.2.b.3B.a

blindness or partial sight, or

9.2.b.3B.b

another disability.

;

9.2.c

after paragraph (7) insert—

9.2.c.8

The Electoral Commission must give guidance to returning officers in relation
to the duty imposed by paragraph (3A)(b).

9.2.c.9

Before giving guidance under paragraph (8), the Commission must consult such
persons, including bodies representing the interests of relevant persons, as
they consider appropriate.

9.2.c.10

In performing the duty imposed by paragraph (3A)(b), a returning officer must
have regard to guidance given under paragraph (8).

9.3

In rule 39 (voting by persons with disabilities)—

9.3.a

in paragraph (2)(b)(i), for “is a qualified person within the meaning of this
rule” substitute  “is aged 18 or over” ;

9.3.b

in paragraph (3), omit the words from “and a person” to the end.

9.4

In the Appendix of Forms, in the form of declaration to be made by the
companion of a voter with disabilities—

9.4.a

for the words from “[I am entitled” to “18 years],” substitute  “I am aged 18
or over” ;

9.4.b

omit “* State the relationship of the companion to the voter.”

9.5

In section 5 of PPERA (reports on elections etc), after subsection (2A)
insert—

9.5.2AA

Subsection (2AB) applies where a report under this section relates to—

9.5.2AA.a

a parliamentary general election,

9.5.2AA.b

a parliamentary by-election,

9.5.2AA.c

an ordinary election of police and crime commissioners,

9.5.2AA.d

an election held under section 51 of the Police Reform and Social
Responsibility Act 2011 (election to fill vacancy in office of police and
crime commissioner), or

9.5.2AA.e

a Northern Ireland Assembly general election.

9.5.2AB

The report must include a description of the steps taken by returning officers
to assist relevant persons (within the meaning of rule 29 of Schedule 1 to the
Representation of the People Act 1983) to vote at the election.

#### Nomination of candidates at parliamentary elections

##### Candidate nomination paper: commonly used names

10

10.1

Schedule 1 to RPA 1983 (Parliamentary elections rules) is amended as follows.

10.2

10.2.2A

If a candidate—

10.2.2A.a

commonly uses a surname that is different from any other surname the candidate
has,

10.2.2A.b

commonly uses a forename that is different from any other forename the
candidate has, or

10.2.2A.c

otherwise commonly uses one or more forenames or a surname in a different way
from the way in which the candidate’s names are stated in accordance with
paragraph (2)(a) (for example, where the commonly used names are in a
different order from the names as so stated, include only some of those names,
or include additional names),

the nomination paper may state the commonly used name or names in addition to
the names as stated in accordance with paragraph (2)(a).

10.3

10.3.a

;

substitute—

10.4.2A

Where a candidate commonly uses a name or names—

10.4.2A.a

that are different from the candidate’s full names as stated on the nomination
paper, or

10.4.2A.b

in a different way from the candidate’s full names as stated on the nomination
paper,

the commonly used name or names may also appear on the nomination paper; but
if they do so, the commonly used name or names (instead of any other name)
will appear on the ballot paper.

### Overseas electors and EU citizens

#### Overseas electors

##### Extension of franchise for parliamentary elections: British citizens overseas

14

14.1

For sections 1 and 2 of the Representation of the People Act 1985 substitute—

########### Extension of parliamentary franchise

14.1.1

14.1.1.1

A person is entitled to vote as an elector at a parliamentary election in a
constituency if—

14.1.1.1.a

on the declaration date, the person—

14.1.1.1.a.i

qualifies as an overseas elector in respect of that constituency (see section
1A),

14.1.1.1.a.ii

is not subject to any legal incapacity to vote (age apart), and

14.1.1.1.a.iii

is a British citizen, and

14.1.1.1.b

on the date of the poll, the person—

14.1.1.1.b.i

is not subject to any legal incapacity to vote,

14.1.1.1.b.ii

is a British citizen, and

14.1.1.1.b.iii

is registered in a register of parliamentary electors for that constituency.

14.1.1.2

In this section, “ the declaration date ” means—

14.1.1.2.a

the date on which the person makes a declaration under and in accordance with
section 1C  (overseas elector’s declaration), or

14.1.1.2.b

where the person makes a declaration under and in accordance with  section 1E
(renewal declaration), the date on which the person makes the declaration.

########### Qualification as an overseas elector in respect of a constituency

14.1.1A

14.1.1A.1

For the purposes of this Act and the principal Act, a person qualifies as an
overseas elector in respect of a constituency on the declaration date if—

14.1.1A.1.a

on that date the person is not resident in the United Kingdom, and

14.1.1A.1.b

the person satisfies the previous registration condition or the previous
residence condition.

14.1.1A.2

A person satisfies the previous registration condition if—

14.1.1A.2.a

the person has at some time in the past been entered in an electoral register
in respect of an address at a place that is situated within the constituency,
and

14.1.1A.2.b

subsequent to that entry ceasing to have effect, the person has not been
included in any electoral register (whether in respect of the address
mentioned in paragraph (a) or any other address).

14.1.1A.3

A person satisfies the previous residence condition if—

14.1.1A.3.a

the person has at some time in the past been resident in the United Kingdom,

14.1.1A.3.b

on the last day on which the person was resident in the United Kingdom, the
person—

14.1.1A.3.b.i

was resident at an address at a place that is situated within the
constituency, or

14.1.1A.3.b.ii

was not so resident but could have made a declaration under section 7B of the
principal Act (a “declaration of local connection”) in respect of such an
address, and

14.1.1A.3.c

subject to  section 1B (4) , the person has not at any time been included in
any electoral register (whether in respect of the address mentioned in
paragraph (b)  or any other address).

14.1.1A.4

For the purposes of  subsection (3) (b) (ii) , it is to be assumed that
section 7B of the principal Act was in force on the last day on which the
person was resident in the United Kingdom.

14.1.1A.5

In this section—

            “ declaration date ” has the same meaning as in  section 1 ;
“ electoral register ” means—
a register of parliamentary electors, or
a register of local government electors (including a register of electors
prepared for the purposes of local elections (within the meaning of the
Electoral Law Act (Northern Ireland) 1962)).

########### British citizens overseas: entitlement to be registered

14.1.1B

14.1.1B.1

A person is entitled to be registered in a register of parliamentary electors
in pursuance of a declaration made by the person under and in accordance with
section 1C  (an “overseas elector’s declaration”) if the following two
conditions are satisfied.

14.1.1B.2

The first condition is that the register is for the constituency or part of
the constituency within which is situated the place of the address specified
in the declaration by virtue of—

14.1.1B.2.a

section 1C (2) (a)  (where the person is seeking to be registered in reliance
on the previous registration condition), or

14.1.1B.2.b

section 1C (3) (a)  or  (4)  (where the person is seeking to be registered in
reliance on the previous residence condition).

14.1.1B.3

The second condition is that the registration officer concerned is satisfied
that, on the date on which the person makes the declaration, the person
qualifies as an overseas elector in respect of the constituency.

14.1.1B.4

Where—

14.1.1B.4.a

a person applies to be registered in a register of parliamentary electors in
reliance on the previous residence condition, and

14.1.1B.4.b

the registration officer concerned considers that insufficient evidence is
available for the purpose of determining whether the person has at any time
been included in any electoral register (within the meaning of  section 1A ),

the officer may disregard  section 1A (3) (c)  in determining whether the
person satisfies the previous residence condition.

14.1.1B.5

An overseas elector’s declaration made by a person is of no effect unless
received by the registration officer concerned within the period of 3 months
beginning with the date on which the person makes the declaration.

14.1.1B.6

For the purposes of  section 1A , where a person is registered in a register
of parliamentary electors for a constituency or part of a constituency in
pursuance of an overseas elector’s declaration, it is to be conclusively
presumed that the person was not resident in the United Kingdom on the date on
which the person made the declaration.

14.1.1B.7

See also sections 10ZC and 10A of the principal Act, which (among other
things) contain provision about the making of applications for registration.

########### Overseas elector’s declaration

14.1.1C

14.1.1C.1

An overseas elector’s declaration must—

14.1.1C.1.a

give the full name of the person making the declaration (“the declarant”),

14.1.1C.1.b

state the date of the declaration,

14.1.1C.1.c

state that the declarant is a British citizen,

14.1.1C.1.d

state that the declarant is not resident in the United Kingdom on the date of
the declaration,

14.1.1C.1.e

state whether the declarant is seeking to be registered in reliance on the
previous registration condition or the previous residence condition,

14.1.1C.1.f

contain any other prescribed information and satisfy any other prescribed
requirements (which may include requirements for the declaration to be
attested), and

14.1.1C.1.g

state that the declarant believes the matters stated in the declaration to be
true.

14.1.1C.2

Where the declarant is seeking to be registered in reliance on the previous
registration condition, the declaration must also—

14.1.1C.2.a

specify—

14.1.1C.2.a.i

the address in the United Kingdom in respect of which the declarant was
included in an electoral register, and

14.1.1C.2.a.ii

when the declarant was last included in such a register in respect of that
address, and

14.1.1C.2.b

state that since the declarant’s entry in that register in respect of that
address ceased to have effect, the declarant has not been included in any
electoral register (whether in respect of that or any other address).

14.1.1C.3

Where the declarant is seeking to be registered in reliance on the previous
residence condition by virtue of  section 1A (3) (b) (i) , the declaration
must also—

14.1.1C.3.a

specify—

14.1.1C.3.a.i

the address in the United Kingdom at which the declarant was resident, and

14.1.1C.3.a.ii

when the declarant was last resident at that address, and

14.1.1C.3.b

state that since being resident at that address, the declarant has not been
resident at any other address in the United Kingdom.

14.1.1C.4

Where the declarant is seeking to be registered in reliance on the previous
residence condition by virtue of  section 1A (3) (b) (ii) , the declaration
must also specify an address in respect of which the declarant could have made
a declaration of local connection on the last day on which the declarant was
resident in the United Kingdom.

14.1.1C.5

An overseas elector’s declaration that specifies an address in Northern
Ireland under  subsection (2) (a) ,  (3) (a)  or  (4)  may, instead of or in
addition to including a statement under  subsection (1) (c) , state that the
declarant is an Irish citizen who—

14.1.1C.5.a

was born in Northern Ireland, and

14.1.1C.5.b

qualifies as a British citizen (whether or not the declarant identifies as
such).

14.1.1C.6

If the declarant—

14.1.1C.6.a

makes an overseas elector’s declaration that specifies more than one address
under  subsection (2) (a) ,  (3) (a)  or  (4) , or

14.1.1C.6.b

makes two or more overseas elector’s declarations that bear the same date and
specify different addresses in the United Kingdom under  subsection (2) (a) ,
(3) (a)  or  (4) ,

the declaration or declarations are void.

14.1.1C.7

The declarant may at any time cancel an overseas elector’s declaration made by
the declarant.

14.1.1C.8

In this section—

            “ electoral register ” has the same meaning as in  section 1A ;
“ registered ” means registered in a register of parliamentary electors.

14.1.1C.9

A person found abandoned in Northern Ireland as a new-born infant is, unless
the contrary is shown, deemed for the purposes of  subsection (5)  to have
been born in Northern Ireland.

########### Duration of entitlement to be registered

14.1.1D

14.1.1D.1

Where a person is registered in a register of parliamentary electors in
pursuance of an overseas elector’s declaration, the person is entitled to
remain so registered until—

14.1.1D.1.a

the third 1 November following the date when the person’s entry on the
register first takes effect (subject to any extension under subsections  (2)
and  (3) ), or

14.1.1D.1.b

if sooner, the occurrence of an event mentioned in  subsection (4) .

14.1.1D.2

Subsection (3)  applies if—

14.1.1D.2.a

at any time during the 6 months ending with the last day of the initial
registration period or of any further registration period, the registration
officer concerned receives a declaration made by the person under and in
accordance with  section 1E  (a “renewal declaration”), and

14.1.1D.2.b

the registration officer is satisfied that, on the date on which the person
makes the renewal declaration, the person is entitled to remain registered in
the register in pursuance of the overseas elector’s declaration.

14.1.1D.3

The person is entitled to remain registered in the register in pursuance of
the overseas elector’s declaration until—

14.1.1D.3.a

the third 1 November following the day after the last day of the initial
registration period or of the further registration period in question (subject
to any further extension), or

14.1.1D.3.b

if sooner, the occurrence of an event specified in  subsection (4) .

14.1.1D.4

The events referred to in  subsections (1) (b)  and  (3) (b)  are—

14.1.1D.4.a

the registration officer determines in accordance with regulations that the
person was not entitled to be registered or to remain registered (as the case
may be);

14.1.1D.4.b

the registration officer determines in accordance with regulations—

14.1.1D.4.b.i

that the person was registered as the result of an application under section
10ZC or 10A(1) of the principal Act made by some other person, or

14.1.1D.4.b.ii

that the person’s entry has been altered as the result of an application under
section 10ZD or 10A(4) of that Act made by some other person;

14.1.1D.4.c

the overseas elector’s declaration is cancelled (see section  1C (7) );

14.1.1D.4.d

another entry made in respect of the person in any electoral register takes
effect (in the case of a register of parliamentary electors, whether or not in
pursuance of an overseas elector’s declaration).

14.1.1D.5

A renewal declaration made by a person is of no effect unless received by the
registration officer concerned within the period of 3 months beginning with
the date on which the person makes the declaration.

14.1.1D.6

In this section—

            “ electoral register ” has the same meaning as in  section 1A ;
“ initial registration period ” means the period for which the person is
entitled by virtue of  subsection (1) (a)  to remain registered;
“ further registration period ” means a period for which the person is
entitled by virtue of  subsection (3) (a)  to remain registered.

14.1.1D.7

Where a person is entitled to remain registered in a register of parliamentary
electors for a constituency or part of a constituency by virtue of subsections
(2)  and  (3) , it is to be conclusively presumed for the purposes of  section
1A  that the person was not resident in the United Kingdom on the date on
which the person made the renewal declaration in question.

14.1.1D.8

Where a person’s entitlement to remain registered in a register of
parliamentary electors terminates by virtue of  subsection (1)  or  (3) , the
registration officer concerned must remove the person’s entry from the
register.

########### Renewal declaration

14.1.1E

14.1.1E.1

A renewal declaration must—

14.1.1E.1.a

give the full name and date of birth of the person making the declaration
(“the declarant”),

14.1.1E.1.b

state the date of the declaration,

14.1.1E.1.c

state that the declarant is a British citizen,

14.1.1E.1.d

state that the declarant is not resident in the United Kingdom on the date of
the declaration,

14.1.1E.1.e

contain any other prescribed information and satisfy any other prescribed
requirements, and

14.1.1E.1.f

state that the declarant believes the matters stated in the declaration to be
true.

14.1.1E.2

A renewal declaration must also—

14.1.1E.2.a

specify the address in respect of which the declarant is registered, and

14.1.1E.2.b

state that since the declarant was registered in respect of that address, no
other entry has been made in respect of the declarant in any electoral
register (whether in respect of the address mentioned in  paragraph (a)  or
any other address).

14.1.1E.3

A renewal declaration that specifies an address in Northern Ireland under
subsection (2) (a)  may, instead of or in addition to the statement under
subsection (1) (c) , state that the declarant is an Irish citizen who—

14.1.1E.3.a

was born in Northern Ireland, and

14.1.1E.3.b

qualifies as a British citizen (whether or not the declarant identifies as
such),

(and  section 1C (9)  applies as it applies for the purposes of  section 1C
(5) ).

14.1.1E.4

If the declarant—

14.1.1E.4.a

makes a renewal declaration that specifies more than one address under
subsection (2) (a) , or

14.1.1E.4.b

makes two or more renewal declarations that bear the same date and specify
different addresses under  subsection (2) (a) ,

the declaration or declarations are void.

14.1.1E.5

In this section—

            “ electoral register ” has the same meaning as in  section 1A ;
“ registered ” means registered in a register of parliamentary electors in
pursuance of an overseas elector’s declaration.

14.2

Schedule 7  contains amendments and transitional provision relating to this
section.

#### Voting and candidacy rights of EU citizens

15

Schedule 8  makes provision about voting and candidacy rights of EU citizens
in relation to local elections in England and certain other elections.

### The Electoral Commission

#### Strategy and policy statement

##### Strategy and policy statement

16

After section 4 of PPERA insert—

######### Strategy and policy statement

########## Strategy and policy statement

16.4A

16.4A.1

The Secretary of State may designate a statement for the purposes of this
section if the requirements set out in  section 4C  (consultation and
procedural requirements) are satisfied.

16.4A.2

The statement is a statement prepared by the Secretary of State that sets out—

16.4A.2.a

strategic and policy priorities of Her Majesty’s government relating to
elections, referendums and other matters in respect of which the Commission
have functions, and

16.4A.2.b

the role and responsibilities of the Commission in enabling Her Majesty’s
government to meet those priorities.

16.4A.3

The statement may also set out—

16.4A.3.a

guidance relating to particular matters in respect of which the Commission
have functions;

16.4A.3.b

any other information (for example, about the roles and responsibilities of
other persons) the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

16.4A.4

In preparing the statement, the Secretary of State must have regard to the
duties imposed on the Commission by section 145(1) (duties with respect to
compliance with controls imposed by this Act).

16.4A.5

The statement must not contain provision about the carrying out by the
Commission of their functions under Schedule 19B (investigatory powers) or
Schedule 19C (civil sanctions) in relation to a particular person.

16.4A.6

The statement must not include provision in relation to elections, referendums
and other matters so far as the provision would relate to the Commission’s
devolved Scottish functions or the Commission’s devolved Welsh functions.

16.4A.7

A statement designated under this section must be published in whatever manner
the Secretary of State considers appropriate.

16.4A.8

For the purposes of subsection  (6) —

16.4A.8.a

the Commission’s “devolved Scottish functions” are the Commission’s functions
in relation to—

16.4A.8.a.i

Scottish Parliamentary general elections, elections held under section 9 of
the Scotland Act 1998 (constituency vacancies), and local government elections
in Scotland, so far as those functions do not relate to reserved matters
within the meaning of the Scotland Act 1998, and

16.4A.8.a.ii

referendums held throughout Scotland in pursuance of provision made by or
under an Act of the Scottish Parliament;

16.4A.8.b

the Commission’s “devolved Welsh functions” are the Commission’s functions in
relation to—

16.4A.8.b.i

general elections of members of Senedd Cymru,

16.4A.8.b.ii

elections held under section 10 of the Government of Wales Act 2006 (elections
for Senedd constituency vacancies),

16.4A.8.b.iii

local government elections in Wales, and

16.4A.8.b.iv

referendums held under Part 2 of the Local Government Act 2000 or Part 4 of
the Local Government (Wales) Measure 2011 (referendums relating to local
authority executive arrangements),

so far as those functions do not relate to reserved matters within the meaning
of the Government of Wales Act 2006.

########## Duties in relation to statement

16.4B

16.4B.1

This section applies where a statement has been designated under  section 4A .

16.4B.2

The Commission must have regard to the statement when carrying out their
functions.

16.4B.3

Subsection (2)  does not apply to information contained in the statement by
virtue of  section 4A (3) (b) .

16.4B.4

The Commission must publish a report, as soon as practicable after the end of—

16.4B.4.a

the period of 12 months beginning with the day on which the statement was
first designated under  section 4A , and

16.4B.4.b

every subsequent 12-month period,

on what they have done during the period in question in consequence of the
statement.

16.4B.5

Where, before the end of a reporting period, the statement is designated by
virtue of  section 4D  (5-yearly review) or  section 4E  (power to revise
statement)—

16.4B.5.a

the Commission are not required to publish a report under  subsection (4)  in
relation to the reporting period, and

16.4B.5.b

subsection (4)  has effect as if the reference in  paragraph (a)  to the day
on which the statement was first designated under  section 4A  were to the day
on which the statement was last designated under that section by virtue of
section 4D  or  4E .

16.4B.6

“ Reporting period ” means a period in relation to which a report is required
to be published under  subsection (4) .

16.4B.7

The duty under  subsection (4)  does not apply in relation to a 12-month
period if before the end of that period the statement’s designation is
withdrawn under  section 4D (4) (c)  or treated as withdrawn under  section 4D
(5) (b) .

16.4B.8

The Commission must provide a copy of each report published under  subsection
(4)  to the Speaker’s Committee.

########## Consultation and procedural requirements

16.4C

16.4C.1

This section sets out the requirements that must be satisfied before the
Secretary of State may designate a statement under  section 4A .

16.4C.2

The Secretary of State must consult the following on a draft of the statement—

16.4C.2.a

the Commission,

16.4C.2.b

the Speaker’s Committee, and

16.4C.2.c

the Levelling Up, Housing and Communities Committee.

16.4C.3

After the Secretary of State has carried out the consultation required by
subsection (2) , the Secretary of State—

16.4C.3.a

must make whatever changes to the draft the Secretary of State considers
necessary in light of responses to the consultation, and

16.4C.3.b

must prepare a report containing the Secretary of State’s response to the
consultation.

16.4C.4

If, after complying with subsection  (3) , the Secretary of State proposes to
designate the statement, the Secretary of State must lay before Parliament a
document that—

16.4C.4.a

explains the Secretary of State’s proposals,

16.4C.4.b

sets them out in the form of a draft statement, and

16.4C.4.c

contains the report prepared under subsection  (3) (b) .

16.4C.5

Where a document is laid before Parliament under subsection  (4) , no draft of
the statement that the Secretary of State proposes to designate is to be laid
before Parliament before the end of the 60-day period.

16.4C.6

In preparing a draft statement for laying before Parliament, the Secretary of
State must consider any representations made during the 60-day period in
relation to anything in the document laid under subsection  (4) .

16.4C.7

If, after the end of the 60-day period, the Secretary of State wishes to
proceed with designating the statement, the Secretary of State must lay before
Parliament—

16.4C.7.a

the draft statement (incorporating any changes made in light of any
representations made as mentioned in subsection  (6) ), and

16.4C.7.b

a report containing the Secretary of State’s response to any such
representations.

16.4C.8

The draft as laid under  subsection (7)  must, before the end of the 40-day
period, have been approved by a resolution of each House of Parliament before
the Secretary of State may designate the statement under  section 4A .

16.4C.9

In this section—

16.4C.9.a

“ the 40-day period ” means the period of 40 days beginning on the day on
which the draft is laid before Parliament (or, if it is not laid before each
House of Parliament on the same day, the later of the days on which it is
laid);

16.4C.9.b

“ the 60-day period ” means the period of 60 days beginning on the day on
which the document mentioned in subsection  (4)  is laid before Parliament
(or, if it is not laid before each House of Parliament on the same day, the
later of the days on which it is laid).

16.4C.10

When calculating the 40-day period or the 60-day period for the purposes of
subsection (9) (a)  or  (b)  respectively, ignore any period during which
Parliament is dissolved or prorogued or during which both Houses are adjourned
for more than 4 days.

16.4C.11

If the name of the Levelling Up, Housing and Communities Committee is changed,
the reference in subsection  (2) (c)  to that Committee is to be read (subject
to subsection  (12) ) as a reference to the Committee by its new name.

16.4C.12

If the functions of the Levelling Up, Housing and Communities Committee at the
passing of this Act with respect to electoral matters (or functions
corresponding substantially to such matters) become functions of a different
committee of the House of Commons, the reference in subsection  (2) (c)  to
that Committee is to be read as a reference to the committee which for the
time being has those functions.

########## 5-yearly review and designation of statement

16.4D

16.4D.1

The Secretary of State must review a statement designated under  section 4A
if a period of 5 years has elapsed since—

16.4D.1.a

the time when the statement was first designated under  section 4A , or

16.4D.1.b

if later, the time when the statement was last designated under that section
by virtue of this section or  section 4E .

16.4D.2

But where—

16.4D.2.a

the statement was last designated by virtue of  section 4E , and

16.4D.2.b

the case was one in which the Secretary of State made a determination under
section 4E (5)  (disapplication of consultation and other pre-designation
requirements on revision of statement),

the designation of the statement in that case is to be ignored in determining
for the purposes of  subsection (1) (b)  when the statement was last
designated.

16.4D.3

A review under  subsection (1)  must take place as soon as reasonably
practicable after the end of the 5-year period referred to in that subsection.

16.4D.4

After reviewing the statement, the Secretary of State may—

16.4D.4.a

revise the statement,

16.4D.4.b

leave the statement as it is, or

16.4D.4.c

withdraw the statement’s designation under  section 4A .

16.4D.5

Where the Secretary of State proceeds under  subsection (4) (a)  or  (b) —

16.4D.5.a

the Secretary of State must designate the statement (whether or not revised)
under  section 4A (1) ;

16.4D.5.b

if the statement is not designated before the end of the review period, the
designation of the statement (in the form reviewed under  subsection (1) ) is
treated as withdrawn at the end of that period.

16.4D.6

“ The review period ” means the 12 months beginning with the end of the 5-year
period referred to in  subsection (1) .

16.4D.7

Sections  4A (2)  to  (7)  and  4C  apply in relation to the statement and its
designation in accordance with  subsection (5) (a)  as they apply in relation
to the original statement.

########## Power to revise statement

16.4E

16.4E.1

The Secretary of State may revise a statement designated under  section 4A
otherwise than in consequence of a review under  section 4D .

16.4E.2

The power under  subsection (1)  may be exercised—

16.4E.2.a

on the Secretary of State’s own initiative,

16.4E.2.b

at the request of the Commission, where the request—

16.4E.2.b.i

is made by notice given to the Secretary of State and the Speaker’s Committee,
and

16.4E.2.b.ii

gives details of the changes to the statement that the Commission propose
should be made, or

16.4E.2.c

at the request of the Speaker’s Committee, where the request—

16.4E.2.c.i

is made by notice given to the Secretary of State, and

16.4E.2.c.ii

gives details of the changes to the statement that the Speaker’s Committee
propose should be made.

16.4E.3

Where a request is made in accordance with subsection  (2) (b)  or  (c) , the
Secretary of State must inform the Commission or the Speaker’s Committee (as
the case may be) how the Secretary of State proposes to deal with the request.

16.4E.4

Where the Secretary of State revises the statement under  subsection (1) —

16.4E.4.a

the Secretary of State must designate the revised statement under  section 4A
(1) , and

16.4E.4.b

subject to  subsection (5) , sections  4A (2)  to  (7)  and  4C  apply to the
revised statement and its designation in accordance with  paragraph (a)  as
they apply to the original statement.

16.4E.5

The Secretary of State may determine in a particular case that  section 4C (2)
to  (6)  (consultation and pre-designation requirements) does not apply in
relation to the revised statement.

16.4E.6

Before making a determination under  subsection (5) , the Secretary of State—

16.4E.6.a

must give notice to the Speaker’s Committee of the proposed determination
(giving details of the revisions to the statement), and

16.4E.6.b

must consider any representations made by the Speaker’s Committee in response
to the notice.

16.4E.7

Where the Secretary of State makes a determination under  subsection (5) , the
Secretary of State must notify the following of the revisions to the
statement—

16.4E.7.a

the Commission,

16.4E.7.b

the Speaker’s Committee, and

16.4E.7.c

the Levelling Up, Housing and Communities Committee,

and section  4C (11)  and  (12)  apply for the purposes of paragraph  (c)  as
they apply for the purposes of  section 4C (2) (c) .

16.4E.8

Subsection (9)  applies where the Secretary of State makes a determination
under  subsection (5)  despite the Speaker’s Committee objecting to the
proposed determination.

16.4E.9

When laying the revised statement before Parliament in accordance with
section 4C (7) (a) , the Secretary of State must also lay before Parliament a
statement of the Secretary of State’s reasons for the determination.

16.4E.10

For the purposes of this section, corrections of clerical or typographical
errors do not count as a revision of the statement.

##### Examination of duty to have regard to strategy and policy statement

17

17.1

After section 13 of PPERA insert—

########### Examination of Commission’s duty to have regard to strategy and policy statement

############ Examination of duty to have regard to strategy and policy statement

17.1.13ZA

17.1.13ZA.1

The Speaker’s Committee may examine the performance by the Commission of the
Commission’s duty under  section 4B (2)  (duty to have regard to strategy and
policy statement).

17.1.13ZA.2

The Speaker’s Committee may require the Commission to provide the Committee
with information that—

17.1.13ZA.2.a

the Committee require for the purposes of enabling them to exercise their
power under  subsection (1) , and

17.1.13ZA.2.b

is held by the Commission.

17.1.13ZA.3

The Commission—

17.1.13ZA.3.a

must as soon as is reasonably practicable provide the Speaker’s Committee with
information required under  subsection (2) , and

17.1.13ZA.3.b

must provide the information in such form as the Committee may reasonably
require.

17.1.13ZA.4

A requirement imposed on the Commission under  subsection (2)  does not
require the Commission to provide information that, in their opinion, might
adversely affect any current investigation or proceedings.

17.1.13ZA.5

Except as provided by subsection  (6) , the disclosure of information pursuant
to a requirement imposed under  subsection (2)  does not breach—

17.1.13ZA.5.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the Commission, or

17.1.13ZA.5.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

17.1.13ZA.6

A requirement imposed on the Commission under  subsection (2)  does not
require them to disclose information if to do so would contravene the data
protection legislation (but, in determining whether a disclosure would do so,
the requirement imposed on the Commission is to be taken into account).

17.1.13ZA.7

In  subsection (6) , “ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning
as in the Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 3(9) of that Act).

17.2

In Schedule 2 to PPERA (Speaker’s Committee), after paragraph 3 insert—

########### Protection for witnesses etc

17.2.4

17.2.4.1

Evidence given by a person who is a witness before the Speaker’s Committee may
not be used against the person in any civil or disciplinary proceedings, or in
any criminal proceedings, unless the evidence was given in bad faith.

17.2.4.2

For the purposes of the law of defamation the publication by the Speaker’s
Committee of any evidence given by a person who is a witness before the
Speaker’s Committee is absolutely privileged.

### Regulation of expenditure

#### Notional expenditure of candidates and others

##### Notional expenditure: use of property etc on behalf of candidates and others

20

20.1

In section 90C of RPA 1983 (property, goods, services etc provided free of
charge or at a discount), after subsection (1) insert—

20.1.1A

For the purposes of subsection (1)(b), except as it applies in relation to an
election in Scotland or Wales under the local government Act, property, goods,
services or facilities are made use of on behalf of a candidate only if their
use on behalf of the candidate is directed, authorised or encouraged by the
candidate or the candidate’s election agent.

20.2

In section 73 of PPERA (notional campaign expenditure)—

20.2.a

after subsection (1) insert—

20.2.a.1A

For the purposes of subsection (1)(b), as it applies for the purposes of a
period in relation to which any limit is imposed by paragraph 3, 7, 9, 10 or
11 of Schedule 9 (periods involving parliamentary general elections or general
elections to the Northern Ireland Assembly), property, services or facilities
are made use of on behalf of a registered party only if their use on behalf of
the party is directed, authorised or encouraged by—

20.2.a.1A.a

the party, or

20.2.a.1A.b

the treasurer or a deputy treasurer appointed under section 74.

;

20.2.b

in subsection (10), after “(1),” insert  “(1A),” .

20.3

In section 86 of PPERA (notional controlled expenditure), after subsection (1)
insert—

20.3.1A

For the purposes of subsection (1)(b), as it applies for the purposes of a
period in relation to which any limit is imposed by paragraph 3, 7, 9, 10 or
11 of Schedule 10 (periods involving parliamentary general elections or
general elections to the Northern Ireland Assembly), property, services or
facilities are made use of on behalf of a third party only if their use on
behalf of the third party is directed, authorised or encouraged by the third
party or (where the third party is a recognised third party and is not an
individual) by the third party or the responsible person.

20.4

In section 94 of PPERA (limits on controlled expenditure by third parties),
after subsection (8) insert—

20.4.8A

Where the period is one in relation to which any limit is imposed by paragraph
3, 7, 9, 10 or 11 of Schedule 10 (periods involving parliamentary general
elections or general elections to the Northern Ireland Assembly), property,
services or facilities are made use of on behalf of a third party for the
purposes of subsection (8)(b) only if their use on behalf of the third party
is directed, authorised or encouraged by the third party or (where the third
party is a recognised third party and is not an individual) by the third party
or the responsible person.

20.5

In section 112 of PPERA (notional referendum expenses), after subsection (1)
insert—

20.5.1A

For the purposes of subsection (1)(b), property, services or facilities are
made use of on behalf of an individual or body only if their use on behalf of
the individual or body is directed, authorised or encouraged by the individual
or body or (where the individual or body is a permitted participant) by the
individual or body or the responsible person.

20.6

In paragraph 6 of Schedule 3 to the Recall of MPs Act 2015 (regulation of
expenditure: notional petition expenses), after sub-paragraph (3) insert—

20.6.3A

For the purposes of sub-paragraph (3), property, services or facilities are
made use of on behalf of P only if their use on behalf of P is directed,
authorised or encouraged by P or (where P is an accredited campaigner) by P or
the responsible person.

20.7

In section 52B of the  Electoral Law Act (Northern Ireland) 1962 (c. 14
(N.I.))  (property, goods, services etc provided free of charge or at a
discount), after subsection (1) insert—

20.7.1A

For the purposes of subsection (1)(b), property, goods, services or facilities
are made use of on behalf of a candidate only if their use on behalf of the
candidate is directed, authorised or encouraged by the candidate or the
candidate’s election agent.

##### Section 24: transitional provision

25

25.1

If controlled expenditure is incurred by or on behalf of a relevant person
during any post-commencement period in relation to which any limit is imposed
by Schedule 10 to PPERA (limits on controlled expenditure), no campaign
expenditure may be incurred during that period by or on behalf of the person.

25.2

“ Relevant person ” means a person who, immediately before the commencement
date, is both a registered party and a recognised third party.

25.3

Where campaign expenditure is incurred by or on behalf of a relevant person in
contravention of subsection  (1) , section 79(2) of PPERA (offence for
exceeding limit on campaign expenditure) applies as if campaign expenditure
had been incurred in excess of any limit imposed by Schedule 9 to PPERA (and
for this purpose references in section 79(2) of PPERA to a registered party
are to be read as references to the relevant person in its capacity as a
registered party).

25.4

See also  section 89A  of PPERA (inserted by section 26 below), which among
other things restricts the incurring of controlled expenditure by or on behalf
of a registered party which is also a third party.

25.5

A third party may not give a notification under section 88(4)(b) of PPERA
(recognised third parties: renewal of original notification) on or after the
commencement date if it is also a registered party.

25.6

In this section—

                                    “ campaign expenditure ” has the same
meaning as it has for the purposes of Part 5 of PPERA (see section 72(2) of
that Act);
“ the commencement date ” means the date on which this section comes into
force (and post-commencement, in relation to a period, means beginning on or
after that date);
“ controlled expenditure ”, “ recognised third party ” and “ third party ”
have the same meaning as they have for the purposes of Part 6 of PPERA (see
section 85 of that Act);
“ registered party ” has the same meaning as in PPERA (see section 160(1) of
that Act).

#### Controlled expenditure etc

##### Restriction on which third parties may incur controlled expenditure

26

26.1

In Part 6 of PPERA, at the beginning of Chapter 2 insert—

########### Which third parties may incur expenditure

############ Restriction on which third parties may incur controlled expenditure

26.1.89A

26.1.89A.1

No amount of controlled expenditure may be incurred by or on behalf of a third
party during a reserved regulated period unless the third party—

26.1.89A.1.a

falls within any paragraph of section 88(2) (third parties eligible to give
notification), or

26.1.89A.1.b

is an unincorporated association with the requisite UK connection.

26.1.89A.2

Subsection (1) does not apply to any expenses incurred by or on behalf of a
third party during a reserved regulated period which do not in total exceed
£700.

26.1.89A.3

Subsections (4) and (5) apply where expenses are incurred by or on behalf of a
third party in contravention of subsection (1).

26.1.89A.4

If the third party is not an individual—

26.1.89A.4.a

any person who authorised the expenses to be incurred by or on behalf of the
third party is guilty of an offence if the person knew or ought reasonably to
have known that the expenses would be incurred in contravention of subsection
(1), and

26.1.89A.4.b

the third party is also guilty of an offence.

26.1.89A.5

If the third party is an individual, the individual is guilty of an offence if
they knew or ought reasonably to have known that the expenses would be
incurred in contravention of subsection (1).

26.1.89A.6

An unincorporated association has “the requisite UK connection” if it consists
of two or more persons both or all of whom are registered in a register of
parliamentary electors in pursuance of a declaration made under and in
accordance with section 1C of the Representation of the People Act 1985
(overseas elector’s declaration).

26.1.89A.7

In this section—

                     “ register of parliamentary electors ” means a register
of parliamentary electors maintained under section 9 of the Representation of
the People Act 1983;
“ reserved regulated period ” means a period in relation to which any limit is
imposed by paragraph 3, 7, 9, 10 or 11 of Schedule 10 (periods involving
parliamentary general elections or general elections to the Northern Ireland
Assembly).

26.2

insert—

 Section 89A(4) or (5) (incurring controlled expenditure in contravention of
section 89A(1)) On summary conviction in England and Wales: fine On summary
conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland: statutory maximum On indictment:
fine

.

this section comes fully into force.

26.4

to which any limit is imposed by paragraph 3, 7, 9, 10 or 11 of Schedule 10 to

##### Recognised third parties: changes to existing limits etc

28

28.1

In section 85 of PPERA (controlled expenditure by third parties), before
subsection (6) insert—

28.1.5B

“ The lower-tier expenditure limits ”, in relation to controlled expenditure
incurred by or on behalf of a recognised third party, means the limits
specified in section 94(5) (limits on controlled expenditure incurred in a
part of the UK); and a recognised third party is subject to those limits if
the notification given by the third party under section 88(1), as it has
effect for the time being, contains a statement within section 88(3D).

28.2

Section 88 of PPERA (third parties recognised for the purposes of Part 6) is
amended in accordance with  subsections (3)  to  (6) .

28.3

After subsection (3C) insert—

28.3.3D

A notification given under subsection (1) by a third party so as to be subject
to the lower-tier expenditure limits must contain a statement to that effect.

28.4

In subsection (6)—

28.4.a

in paragraph (a), after “statements” insert  “within subsection (3)” ;

28.4.b

in paragraph (b)—

28.4.b.i

after “any statement” insert  “within subsection (3)” ;

28.4.b.ii

for “subsection (3)” substitute  “that subsection” .

28.5

After subsection (6) insert—

28.5.6A

In a case where the original notification, as it has effect for the time
being, contains a statement within subsection (3D), the renewal notification
must either—

28.5.6A.a

confirm that the statement is to continue to have effect, or

28.5.6A.b

indicate that the statement is withdrawn.

28.6

In subsection (8), for the words from “any statement” to the end substitute—

28.6.a

any statement within subsection (3) that is contained in the original
notification, as it has effect for the time being, is replaced by some other
statement conforming with that subsection that is contained in the
notification of alteration, or

28.6.b

any statement within subsection (3D) that is contained in the original
notification, as it has effect for the time being, is withdrawn.

28.7

Section 94 of PPERA (limits on controlled expenditure by third parties) is
amended in accordance with  subsections (8)  to  (10) .

28.8

In subsection (3)—

28.8.a

in paragraph (a), for “either” substitute

any of the following sub-paragraphs applies—

28.8.a.ai

during a regulated period in relation to which any limit is imposed by
paragraph 3, 7, 9, 10 or 11 of Schedule 10 (periods involving parliamentary
general elections or general elections to the Northern Ireland Assembly), any
controlled expenditure is incurred by or on behalf of a third party in excess
of £10,000;

;

28.8.b

at the end of paragraph (a)(i), for “, or” substitute  “;” ;

28.8.c

for paragraph (b) substitute—

28.8.c.b

the third party—

28.8.c.b.i

in a case within paragraph (a)(ai) or (ii), is not a recognised third party;

28.8.c.b.ii

in a case within paragraph (a)(i), is not a recognised third party or, where

28.9

28.9.4ZA

In its application to a case within subsection (3)(a)(i) where the third party

28.10

Where an offence under subsection (4) is committed in the case of a recognised

28.10.10A.a

28.10.10A.b

this Part then applies to the third party as if the notification under section

28.11

A recognised third party that is subject to the lower-tier expenditure limits

28.12

28.12.a

28.13
