##### Code of practice on controls relating to third parties

29

29.1

After section 100 of PPERA insert—

########### Code of practice relating to controlled expenditure

############ Code of practice on controlled expenditure

29.1.100A

29.1.100A.1

The Commission must prepare a code of practice about the operation of this
Part in relation to a reserved regulated period.

29.1.100A.2

The code must in particular set out—

29.1.100A.2.a

guidance on the kinds of expenses which do, or do not, fall within Part 1 of
Schedule 8A (qualifying expenses);

29.1.100A.2.b

guidance on determining whether the condition in section 85(2)(b) (promoting
or procuring electoral success) is met in relation to expenditure;

29.1.100A.2.c

guidance on determining whether anything provided to or for the use of a third
party falls to be dealt with in accordance with section 86 (notional
controlled expenditure) or with section 95 and Schedule 11 (donations);

29.1.100A.2.d

examples of when expenditure falls to be dealt with in accordance with section
94(6) (expenditure of a third party in pursuance of an arrangement with one or
more other third parties);

29.1.100A.2.e

guidance about the operation of sections 94D to 94H (targeted controlled
expenditure).

29.1.100A.3

The Commission may from time to time revise the code.

29.1.100A.4

In exercising their functions under this Part, the Commission must have regard
to the code.

29.1.100A.5

It is a defence for a third party charged with an offence under any provision
of this Part, where the offence relates to expenditure incurred or treated as
incurred by a third party during a reserved regulated period, to show—

29.1.100A.5.a

that the code, in the form for the time being issued under section 100B, was
complied with by the third party in determining whether the expenditure is
controlled expenditure for the purposes of this Part, and

29.1.100A.5.b

that the offence would not have been committed on the basis of the controlled
expenditure as determined in accordance with the code.

29.1.100A.6

In this section, “ reserved regulated period ” means a period in relation to
which any limit is imposed by paragraph 3, 7, 9, 10 or 11 of Schedule 10
(regulated periods for parliamentary general elections or general elections to
the Northern Ireland Assembly).

29.1.100A.7

Section 100B sets out consultation and procedural requirements relating to the
code or any revised code.

############ Code of practice: consultation and procedural requirements

29.1.100B

29.1.100B.1

The Commission must consult the following on a draft of a code under section
100A—

29.1.100B.1.a

the Speaker’s Committee;

29.1.100B.1.b

the Levelling Up, Housing and Communities Committee;

29.1.100B.1.c

such other persons as the Commission consider appropriate.

29.1.100B.2

After the Commission have carried out the consultation required by subsection
(1), they must—

29.1.100B.2.a

make whatever modifications to the draft code the Commission consider
necessary in light of responses to the consultation, and

29.1.100B.2.b

submit the draft to the Secretary of State for approval by the Secretary of
State.

29.1.100B.3

The Secretary of State may approve a draft code either without modifications
or with such modifications as the Secretary of State may determine.

29.1.100B.4

Once the Secretary of State has approved a draft code, the Secretary of State
must lay before each House of Parliament a copy of the draft, whether—

29.1.100B.4.a

in its original form, or

29.1.100B.4.b

in a form which incorporates any modifications determined under subsection
(3).

29.1.100B.5

If the draft code incorporates any such modifications, the Secretary of State
must at the same time lay before each House a statement of the Secretary of
State’s reasons for making them.

29.1.100B.6

If, within the 40-day period, either House resolves not to approve the draft,
the Secretary of State must take no further steps in relation to the draft
code.

29.1.100B.7

Subsection (6) does not prevent a new draft code from being laid before
Parliament.

29.1.100B.8

If no resolution of the kind mentioned in subsection (6) is made within the
40-day period—

29.1.100B.8.a

the Secretary of State must issue the code in the form of the draft laid
before Parliament,

29.1.100B.8.b

the Commission must arrange for the code to be published in such manner as
they consider appropriate, and

29.1.100B.8.c

the code comes into force on such day as the Secretary of State may by order
appoint.

29.1.100B.9

References in this section (other than in subsection (1)) to a code or draft
code include a revised code or draft revised code.

29.1.100B.10

In this section, “ the 40-day period ”, in relation to a draft code, means—

29.1.100B.10.a

if the draft is laid before one House on a day later than the day on which it
is laid before the other House, the period of 40 days beginning with the later
of the two days, and

29.1.100B.10.b

in any other case, the period of 40 days beginning with the day on which the
draft is laid before each House, no account being taken of any period during
which Parliament is dissolved or prorogued or during which both Houses are
adjourned for more than four days.

29.1.100B.11

If the name of the Levelling Up, Housing and Communities Committee is changed,
the reference in subsection (1)(b) to that Committee is to be read (subject to
subsection (12)) as a reference to the Committee by its new name.

29.1.100B.12

If the functions of the Levelling Up, Housing and Communities Committee at the
passing of this Act with respect to electoral matters (or functions
corresponding substantially to such matters) become functions of a different
committee of the House of Commons, the reference in subsection (1)(b) to that
Committee is to be read as a reference to the committee which for the time
being has those functions.

29.2

In section 156 of PPERA (orders and regulations), in subsection (3), before
paragraph (a) insert—

29.2.za

an order under section 100B(8);

29.3

In Schedule 8A to PPERA (controlled expenditure: qualifying expenses), in
paragraph 3, after sub-paragraph (10) insert—

29.3.11

This paragraph does not apply in relation to expenses incurred during a period
in relation to which any limit is imposed by paragraph 3, 7, 9, 10 or 11 of
Schedule 10 (regulated periods for parliamentary general elections or general
elections to the Northern Ireland Assembly) (see sections 100A and 100B as
regards expenses incurred during such a period).

### Disqualification of offenders for holding elective office etc

#### Disqualification orders

30

30.1

This section applies where—

30.1.a

a person (“the offender”) is convicted of a  Schedule 9  offence,

30.1.b

the offender was aged 18 or over when the offence was committed, and

30.1.c

the court is satisfied beyond reasonable doubt that the offence is aggravated
by hostility related to persons falling within any of sections 32 to 34.

30.2

The court must, when dealing with the offender for the offence, also make an
order (a “disqualification order”) that the offender is disqualified, for the
period of 5 years beginning with the date on which the order is made—

30.2.a

for being nominated for election to a relevant elective office, and

30.2.b

for being elected to or holding a relevant elective office.

30.3

Subsection  (2)  does not apply where the court considers that there are
particular circumstances relating to the offence or to the offender which
would make it unjust in all the circumstances to make the order; and in such a
case the court must state in open court the reasons for not making the order.

30.4

For the purposes of this section an offence is aggravated by hostility related
to persons falling within any of sections 32 to 34 if—

30.4.a

at the time of committing the offence, or immediately before or after doing
so, the offender demonstrated towards the victim of the offence hostility
based on the victim being (or being presumed to be) a person falling within
any of sections 32 to 34, or

30.4.b

the offence was motivated (wholly or partly) by hostility towards persons
falling within any of those sections in their capacity as such.

30.5

For the purposes of subsection  (4)  it is immaterial whether or not the
offender's hostility is also based, to any extent, on any other factor not
mentioned in that subsection.

30.6

For the purpose of deciding whether to make a disqualification order the court
may consider evidence led by the prosecution and the defence.

30.7

It is immaterial whether evidence led in pursuance of subsection  (6)  would
have been admissible in the proceedings in which the offender was convicted.

30.8

Where a  Schedule 9  offence is found to have been committed—

30.8.a

over a period of 2 or more days, or

30.8.b

at some time during a period of 2 or more days,

it is to be taken for the purposes of subsection  (1) (b)  to have been
committed on the last of those days.

30.9

In this section—

                           “ presumed ” means presumed by the offender;
“ Schedule 9 offence ” means an offence listed in  Schedule 9  (and any
reference in that Schedule to an offence includes a reference to that offence
committed by aiding, abetting, counselling or procuring the commission of that
offence).

#### Vacation of office etc

31

31.1

This section applies where a court makes a disqualification order in respect
of a person who holds a relevant elective office.

31.2

The relevant elective office is, subject to subsection  (3) , vacated at the
appropriate time, namely—

31.2.a

the end of the period of 3 months beginning with the order date, or

31.2.b

if earlier, the end of the period allowed for making an appeal against the
conviction or the making of the order.

31.3

Where, before the appropriate time mentioned in subsection  (2) , the person
appeals against the conviction or the making of the order, the relevant
elective office is vacated at the end of the period of 3 months beginning with
the order date unless—

31.3.a

the appeal is dismissed or abandoned at any earlier time (in which case the
relevant elective office is vacated at that time), or

31.3.b

at any time within that period of 3 months the appeal against the conviction
or the making of the order is upheld (in which case the relevant elective
office is not required to be vacated).

31.4

The person is suspended from performing any of the functions of the relevant
elective office during the period beginning with the order date and ending
with—

31.4.a

the date on which the office is vacated in accordance with this section, or

31.4.b

where subsection  (3) (b)  applies, the date on which the appeal against the
conviction or the making of the order is upheld.

31.5

Where—

31.5.a

a person ceases to hold a relevant elective office in accordance with this
section, but

31.5.b

at any later time the person successfully appeals against the conviction or
the making of the order,

the determination of the appeal does not entitle the person to resume that
office.

31.6

In this section “ order date ” means the date on which the disqualification
order is made by the court.

#### Candidates etc

32

32.1

A person falls within this section if the person is—

32.1.a

a candidate or future candidate at an election for a relevant elective office
or a relevant Scottish elective office, or

32.1.b

a substitute or nominee in relation to the seat of a member of the Northern
Ireland Assembly or of a district council in Northern Ireland.

32.2

The reference in subsection  (1) (a)  to a person who is a candidate at an
election includes a person who is included in a list of candidates submitted
in connection with the election.

32.3

For the purposes of subsection  (1) (a)  a person is a future candidate at an
election for a relevant elective office or a relevant Scottish elective office
if—

32.3.a

the person has been declared, whether by the person or by others, to be a
candidate at the election (and the declaration has not been withdrawn),

32.3.b

the election is the next scheduled election for the office, and

32.3.c

the notice of the election has not been published or, in the case of an
election for the office of member of the House of Commons, the writ for the
election has not been issued.

32.4

For the purposes of subsection  (1) (b)  a person is a substitute—

32.4.a

in relation to the seat of a member of the Northern Ireland Assembly, if the
person—

32.4.a.i

is included in a notice given by the member under article 6A of the 2001 Order
(vacancies arising during an Assembly term: independent members) or, where the
member has given more than one notice under that article, in the last such
notice, or

32.4.a.ii

is being considered by the member for inclusion in such a notice;

32.4.b

in relation to the seat of a member of a district council in Northern Ireland,
if the person—

32.4.b.i

is included in a list of substitutes given by the member under section 11C of
the 1962 Act (substitute lists: independent members) or, where the member has
given more than one list of substitutes under that section, in the latest such
list, or

32.4.b.ii

is being considered by the member for inclusion in such a list.

32.5

For the purposes of subsection  (1) (b)  a person is a nominee—

32.5.a

in relation to the seat of a member of the Northern Ireland Assembly, if the
person—

32.5.a.i

has under article 6B of the 2001 Order (vacancies arising during an Assembly
term: members of registered parties) been nominated by the nominating officer
of a registered party to fill a vacancy in the seat, or

32.5.a.ii

is being considered by the nominating officer of a registered party for
nomination under that article;

32.5.b

in relation to the seat of a member of a district council in Northern Ireland,
if the person—

32.5.b.i

has under section 11E or 11F of the 1962 Act (members for registered parties:
filling casual vacancies) been nominated by the nominated officer of a
registered party to fill a vacancy in the seat, or

32.5.b.ii

is being considered by the nominating officer of a registered party for
nomination under either of those sections.

32.6

For the purposes of subsection  (5) (b)  as it applies in relation to section
11F of the 1962 Act, references to the nominated officer of a registered party
are to be read as references to the nominating officers of each of the
registered parties concerned.

32.7

In this section—

                           “ the 1962 Act ” means the Electoral Law Act
(Northern Ireland) 1962;
“ the 2001 Order ” means the Northern Ireland Assembly (Elections) Order 2001
( S.I. 2001/2599 );
“ nominating officer ”, in relation to a registered party, means the person
registered as the party’s nominating officer under PPERA in the Northern
Ireland register (within the meaning of PPERA);
“ registered party ” means a party registered under PPERA in that register.

#### Holders of relevant elective offices

33

33.1

A person falls within this section if the person holds a relevant elective
office or a relevant Scottish elective office.

33.2

For the purposes of subsection  (1)  a person is to be treated as holding a
relevant elective office or a relevant Scottish elective office during any
period when—

33.2.a

the person has been elected as, or declared to be returned as, the holder of
the office, but

33.2.b

their term of office has not yet begun.

#### Campaigners

34

34.1

A person falls within this section if the person is an individual—

34.1.a

who is a permitted participant in relation to a referendum to which Part 7 of
PPERA applies,

34.1.b

who is a recognised third party,

34.1.c

who is involved in the conduct or management of a local referendum campaign,

34.1.d

who is an accredited campaigner in relation to a recall petition, or

34.1.e

who—

34.1.e.i

undertakes activities for election purposes, for referendum purposes or for
recall petition purposes, and

34.1.e.ii

is employed or engaged by a person falling within subsection  (5)  wholly or
partly for the purpose of undertaking such activities.

34.2

Activities are undertaken “for election purposes” if they are undertaken—

34.2.a

for the purposes of or in connection with—

34.2.a.i

promoting or procuring electoral success for a registered party at a relevant
election, or

34.2.a.ii

promoting or procuring the election of a candidate at a relevant election,

34.2.b

for the purposes of or in connection with enhancing the standing with the
electorate, in connection with future relevant elections (whether imminent or
otherwise), of a registered party or a candidate at a relevant election, or

34.2.c

with a view to prejudicing—

34.2.c.i

the electoral prospects of a registered party or a candidate at a relevant
election, or

34.2.c.ii

the standing with the electorate, in connection with future relevant elections
(whether imminent or otherwise), of a registered party or a candidate at a
relevant election.

34.3

Activities are undertaken “for referendum purposes” if they are undertaken—

34.3.a

for the purposes of or in connection with promoting or procuring a particular
outcome in relation to the question asked in a relevant referendum, or

34.3.b

with a view to prejudicing the prospects of another particular outcome in
relation to the question asked in a relevant referendum.

34.4

Activities are undertaken “for recall petition purposes” if they are
undertaken for the purposes of or in connection with promoting or procuring
the success or failure of a recall petition.

34.5

The following persons fall within this subsection—

34.5.a

a registered party;

34.5.b

a person who falls within section 32 (1) (a)  (candidates etc);

34.5.c

a permitted participant in relation to a referendum to which Part 7 of PPERA
applies;

34.5.d

a recognised third party;

34.5.e

a person involved in the conduct or management of a local referendum campaign;

34.5.f

an accredited campaigner in relation to a recall petition.

34.6

In this section—

                           “ accredited campaigner ” has the same meaning as
in the Recall of MPs Act 2015 (see Part 5 of Schedule 3 to that Act);
“ local referendum ” means a referendum under or by virtue of—
Chapter 4 of Part 1A of the Local Government Act 2000 (local authority
governance: England);
Part 2 of the Local Government Act 2000 (local authority governance: Wales);
section 52ZG or 52ZN of the Local Government Finance Act 1992 (referendums in
relation to council tax);
Schedule 4B or 4C to the Town and Country Planning Act 1990 (referendums on
neighbourhood development plans);
“ local referendum campaign ” means a campaign conducted with a view to
promoting or procuring a particular outcome in relation to the question to be
asked in a local referendum;
“ permitted participant ” has the same meaning as in PPERA (see section 105 of
that Act);
“ recall petition ” has the same meaning as in the Recall of MPs Act 2015 (see
section 1 of that Act);
“ recognised third party ” has the meaning given in section 85(5) of PPERA;
“ registered party ” has the same meaning as in PPERA (see section 160 of that
Act);
“ relevant election ” means an election for a relevant elective office or a
relevant Scottish elective office;
“ relevant referendum ” means—
a referendum to which Part 7 of PPERA applies, or
a local referendum.

34.7

In this section a reference to a individual who is “engaged” by a person
falling within subsection  (5)  includes a reference to an individual who is
engaged otherwise than for payment or promise of payment.

#### Election etc of a person to the House of Commons who is subject to a disqualification order

35

35.1

If a person who is subject to a disqualification order is elected as a member
of the House of Commons, the person’s election is void.

35.2

In section 7 of the House of Commons Disqualification Act 1975 (jurisdiction
of Privy Council as to disqualification), after subsection (5) insert—

35.2.6

In this section, a reference to disqualification by this Act includes a
reference to disqualification by virtue of an order under section 30 of the
Elections Act 2022 (disqualification of offenders for holding elective office
etc).

#### Power to amend 

36

36.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend  Schedule 9  by—

36.1.a

adding offences, or

36.1.b

varying or omitting offences listed in the Schedule.

36.2

Regulations under this section are to be made by statutory instrument.

36.3

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this section may not be
made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of each House of Parliament.

#### Interpretation of Part

37

37.1

In this Part—

“ disqualification order ” means an order made under section 30; “ relevant
elective office ” means the office of— member of the House of Commons; member
of Senedd Cymru; member of the Northern Ireland Assembly; member of a local
authority in England, Wales or Northern Ireland; elected mayor (within the
meaning of Part 1A or 2 of the Local Government Act 2000); mayor for the area
of a combined authority established under section 103 of the Local Democracy,
Economic Development and Construction Act 2009;   mayor for the area of a
combined county authority established under section  9 (1)  of the Levelling-
up and Regeneration Act 2023;   Mayor of London; member of the London
Assembly; police and crime commissioner; “ relevant Scottish elective office ”
means the office of— member of the Scottish Parliament, or member of a council
constituted under section 2 of the Local Government etc. (Scotland) Act 1994.

37.2

In the definition of “relevant elective office” in subsection  (1) , “ local
authority ” means—

37.2.a

in relation to England, a county council, a district council, a parish
council, a London borough council or the Council of the Isles of Scilly;

37.2.b

in relation to Wales, a county council, a county borough council or a
community council;

37.2.c

in relation to Northern Ireland, a district council.

#### Minor and consequential amendments

38

Schedule 10  contains minor and consequential amendments.

### Information to be included with electronic material

#### Definitions

##### Definitions relating to electronic material and publication

39

39.1

The following definitions have effect for the purposes of this Part.

39.2

“ Electronic material ” means material in electronic form which consists of or
includes—

39.2.a

text or moving or still images, or

39.2.b

speech or music.

39.3

In this Part “ electronic material ” does not include material to the extent
that it is received by a person in the form of—

39.3.a

a telephone call made to the person at a telephone number allocated to them in
accordance with a national or international numbering plan, or

39.3.b

a Short Message Service text message sent to such a telephone number.

39.4

“ The promoter ”, in relation to electronic material, means the person causing
the material to be published.

39.5

“ Publish ” means make available to the public at large or any section of the
public.

39.6

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section so as to modify
the definition of “electronic material”, “the promoter” or “publish” that for
the time being has effect for the purposes of this Part.

##### Definitions relating to parties etc

40

40.1

The following definitions have effect for the purposes of this Part.

40.2

“ Registered party ” has the same meaning as in PPERA (see section 160 of that
Act).

40.3

“ Recognised third party ” has the meaning given in section 85(5) of PPERA.

40.4

“ Candidate ” means a candidate at an election for a relevant elective office
or a relevant Scottish elective office within the meaning of Part 5, including
a person who is included in a list of candidates submitted in connection with
such an election.

40.5

“ Future candidate ” means a person who is a future candidate at an election
for a relevant elective office or a relevant Scottish elective office as
defined by section 32 (3) .

40.6

“ Elected office-holder ” means a person within section 33.

40.7

“ Referendum campaigner ” means a person who is a permitted participant within
the meaning of Part 7 of PPERA (see section 105 of that Act) in relation to a
referendum to which that Part applies.

40.8

“ Recall petition campaigner ” means a person who is an accredited campaigner
within the meaning of the Recall of MPs Act 2015 (see Part 5 of Schedule 3 to
that Act) in relation to a recall petition.

40.9

“ Recall petition ” has the same meaning as in the Recall of MPs Act 2015 (see
section 1 of that Act).

40.10

Part 5 has effect for the purposes of subsections (4) to (6) as if the
definition of “relevant elective office” in section 37 (1)  included an office
to which a person may be elected by a municipal election in the City, as
defined by section 191(1) of RPA 1983 (municipal elections in the City of
London).

#### Requirements

##### Requirement to include information with electronic material

41

41.1

This section applies to electronic material which—

41.1.a

meets the conditions in section 42 (paid-for electronic material), or

41.1.b

meets the conditions in section 44 (other electronic material).

41.2

Electronic material to which this section applies must not be published
unless, in accordance with this section—

41.2.a

the information mentioned in subsection  (3)  is included as part of the
electronic material, or

41.2.b

if it is not reasonably practicable to comply with paragraph (a), the
information mentioned in that subsection is displayed in text form in a
location that is directly accessible from the electronic material.

41.3

That information is—

41.3.a

the name and address of the promoter of the material, and

41.3.b

the name and address of any person on behalf of whom the material is being
published (and who is not the promoter).

41.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend subsection  (3)  so as to—

41.4.a

add a description of information, or

41.4.b

modify or remove a description of information that is for the time being
specified in that subsection.

41.5

Information is included as part of electronic material for the purposes of
subsection  (2) (a)  only if—

41.5.a

where the material consists of or includes text or moving or still images, it
is displayed in text form as part of that material;

41.5.b

where the material consists only of speech or music, it forms an audible part
of that material.

41.6

Information that is included as part of electronic material—

41.6.a

must be legible or audible (as the case may be) regardless of the device used
to access the material, and

41.6.b

must be such that, if the electronic material were to be republished by a
person who did not alter the material, the information would be retained as
part of the material when republished.

41.7

Information that is directly accessible from electronic material—

41.7.a

must be legible regardless of the device used to access the information, and

41.7.b

must be such that, if the electronic material were to be republished by a
person who did not alter the material, access to the information would be
retained as part of the material when republished.

41.8

This section is subject to—

41.8.a

section 46 (electronic material relating to more than one candidate), and

41.8.b

section 47 (exceptions).

##### Electronic material to which section 41 applies: paid-for material

42

42.1

Section 41 applies to electronic material which meets the following
conditions.

42.2

The first condition is that the sole or primary purpose that the electronic
material can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve is a purpose within
section 43.

42.3

The second condition is that the promoter of the material, or the person on
behalf of whom the material is published, has paid for the material to be
published as an advertisement.

42.4

The reference in subsection  (3)  to a person paying for material to be
published includes the person providing any other form of consideration in
return for the publication of the material.

42.5

Where the material is published on a website or mobile application of the
promoter or the person on behalf of whom the material is published, the
reference in subsection  (3)  to a person paying for material to be published
does not include the person making payments related to setting up, operating
or maintaining the website or mobile application.

42.6

In subsection  (5)  “ mobile application ” means application software designed
and developed for use by the general public on mobile devices such as
smartphones and tablets.

##### Purposes referred to in section 42

43

43.1

This section sets out the purposes referred to in section 42.

43.2

The first purpose is influencing the public, or any section of the public, to
give support to or withhold support from—

43.2.a

a registered party,

43.2.b

registered parties who advocate (or do not advocate) particular policies or
who otherwise fall within a particular category of such parties, or

43.2.c

candidates or future candidates, in their capacity as such, who hold (or do
not hold) particular opinions or who advocate (or do not advocate) particular
policies or who otherwise fall within a particular category of candidates or
future candidates.

43.3

For the purposes of determining whether electronic material can reasonably be
regarded as intended to achieve the purpose mentioned in subsection  (2) , it
is immaterial that it does not expressly mention the name of any party,
candidate or future candidate.

43.4

The second purpose is influencing the public, or any section of the public, to
give support to or withhold support from a particular candidate or particular
future candidate in their capacity as such.

43.5

For the purposes of determining whether electronic material can reasonably be
regarded as intended to achieve the purpose mentioned in subsection  (4) , it
is immaterial that it does not expressly mention the name of any candidate or
future candidate.

43.6

The third purpose is influencing the public, or any section of the public, to
give support to or withhold support from an elected office-holder in their
capacity as such.

43.7

The fourth purpose is influencing the public, or any section of the public, to
give support to or withhold support from elected office-holders, in their
capacity as such, who hold (or do not hold) particular opinions or who
advocate (or do not advocate) particular policies or who otherwise fall within
a particular category of elected office-holders.

43.8

For the purposes of determining whether electronic material can reasonably be
regarded as intended to achieve the purpose mentioned in subsection  (6)  or
(7) , it is immaterial that it does not expressly mention the name of any
elected office-holder.

43.9

The fifth purpose is influencing the public, or any section of the public, to
give support to or withhold support from—

43.9.a

the holding of a referendum in the United Kingdom or any area in the United
Kingdom, or

43.9.b

a particular outcome of such a referendum.

43.10

For the purposes of determining whether electronic material can reasonably be
regarded as intended to achieve the purpose mentioned in subsection  (9) (b) ,
it is immaterial that it does not expressly mention a particular outcome of a
referendum.

##### Electronic material to which section 41 applies: other electronic material

44

44.1

Section 41 applies to electronic material which meets the following
conditions.

44.2

The first condition is that the electronic material—

44.2.a

can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve any purpose within section
45 (whether or not it can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve any
other purpose as well), or

44.2.b

wholly or mainly relates to a referendum to which Part 7 of PPERA applies and
is published during the referendum period (within the meaning of that Part)
for that referendum.

44.3

The second condition is that the promoter of the material or the person on
behalf of whom it is published is—

44.3.a

a registered party,

44.3.b

a recognised third party,

44.3.c

a candidate or future candidate,

44.3.d

an elected office-holder,

44.3.e

a referendum campaigner, or

44.3.f

a recall petition campaigner.

44.4

The third condition is that neither the promoter of the material, nor the
person on behalf of whom the material is published, has paid for the material
to be published as an advertisement.

44.5

Subsections  (4)  to  (6)  of section 42 apply in relation to subsection  (4)
as they apply in relation to subsection  (3)  of that section.

##### Purposes referred to in section 44

45

45.1

This section sets out the purposes referred to in section 44.

45.2

The first purpose is promoting or procuring electoral success at one or more
particular relevant elections for—

45.2.a

a registered party,

45.2.b

registered parties who advocate (or do not advocate) particular policies or
who otherwise fall within a particular category of such parties, or

45.2.c

candidates or future candidates who hold (or do not hold) particular opinions
or who advocate (or do not advocate) particular policies or who otherwise fall
within a particular category of candidates or future candidates.

45.3

For the purposes of subsection  (2) —

45.3.a

the reference to electoral success at a particular relevant election is a
reference—

45.3.a.i

in relation to a registered party, to the return at the election of any
candidate or future candidate who is standing, or is to stand, in the name of
the party or is included, or is to be included, in a list of candidates
submitted by the party in connection with the election, and

45.3.a.ii

in relation to any candidate or future candidate, to their return at the
election, and

45.3.b

the reference to doing any of the things mentioned in that subsection includes
doing so by prejudicing the electoral prospects at the election of other
parties, candidates or future candidates.

45.4

For the purposes of determining whether electronic material can reasonably be
regarded as intended to achieve the purpose mentioned in subsection (2), it is
immaterial that it does not expressly mention the name of any party, candidate
or future candidate.

45.5

The second purpose is promoting or procuring the election of a particular
candidate or particular future candidate at one or more particular elections.

45.6

For the purposes of determining whether electronic material can reasonably be
regarded as intended to achieve the purpose mentioned in subsection  (5) , it
is immaterial that it does not expressly mention the name of any candidate or
future candidate.

45.7

The third purpose is promoting or procuring the success or failure of a recall
petition.

45.8

For the purposes of determining whether any electronic material can reasonably
be regarded as intended to achieve the purpose mentioned in subsection  (7) ,
it is immaterial that it does not expressly mention the name of the member of
the House of Commons to whom the petition relates.

45.9

In this section “ relevant election ” means—

45.9.a

a parliamentary election,

45.9.b

an election to the Scottish Parliament,

45.9.c

an election to Senedd Cymru,    

45.9.d

an election to the Northern Ireland Assembly,

45.9.e

a local government election within the meaning of section 191, 203 or 204 of
the Representation of the People Act 1983,

45.9.f

an election under Part 1A or 2 of the Local Government Act 2000 for the return
of an elected mayor,

45.9.g

an election for the return of a mayor for the area of a combined authority
established under section 103 of the Local Democracy, Economic Development and
Construction Act 2009,

45.9.ga

an election for the return of a mayor for the area of a combined county
authority established under section  9 (1)  of the Levelling-up and
Regeneration Act 2023,

45.9.h

a local election within the meaning of the Electoral Law Act (Northern
Ireland) 1962 (see section 130(1) of that Act), or

45.9.i

an election of a police and crime commissioner.

##### Electronic material relating to more than one candidate or future candidate

46

46.1

For the purposes of section 41 as it has effect by virtue of sections 42 and
43, electronic material to which subsection  (2)  applies—

46.1.a

is not to be regarded as being published on behalf of a candidate or future
candidate merely because it can be regarded as influencing the public, or any
section of the public, to give support to or withhold support from the
candidate or future candidate, but

46.1.b

may be regarded as being published on behalf of the party mentioned in
subsection  (2) .

46.2

This subsection applies to electronic material which can reasonably be
regarded as influencing the public, or any section of the public, to give
support to or withhold support from—

46.2.a

two or more candidates or future candidates who are standing, or are to stand,
in the name of a party, or

46.2.b

two or more candidates or future candidates who are included, or are to be
included, in a list of candidates submitted by the party in connection with an
election.

46.3

For the purposes of section 41 as it has effect by virtue of sections 44 and
45, electronic material to which subsection  (4)  applies—

46.3.a

is not to be regarded as being published on behalf of a candidate or future
candidate merely because it can be regarded as promoting or procuring the
election of a candidate or future candidate at an election, but

46.3.b

may be regarded as being published on behalf of the party mentioned in
subsection  (4) .

46.4

This subsection applies to electronic material which can reasonably be
regarded as promoting or procuring the election of—

46.4.a

two or more candidates or future candidates who are standing, or are to stand,
in the name of a party, or

46.4.b

two or more candidates or future candidates who are included, or are to be
included, in a list of candidates submitted by the party in connection with an
election.

##### Exceptions to section 41

47

47.1

Section 41 does not apply to the republication of electronic material if—

47.1.a

when it was previously published—

47.1.a.i

section 41 applied to it, and

47.1.a.ii

it was published in compliance with that section, and

47.1.b

it is not materially altered when it is republished.

47.2

In subsection  (1) (b)  the reference to electronic material not being
materially altered includes a reference to the electronic material retaining—

47.2.a

the information within section 41 (3) , or

47.2.b

the access to such information,

as a result of which its previous publication complied with section 41.

47.3

Section 41 does not apply to the publication of electronic material on a
website or mobile application whose primary purpose, or one of whose primary
purposes, is the publication of journalism created for publication on the
website or mobile application, unless the electronic material consists of an
advertisement.

47.4

In subsection  (3)  “ mobile application ” means application software designed
and developed for use by the general public on mobile devices such as
smartphones and tablets.

47.5

Section 41 does not apply to any party political broadcast or referendum
campaign broadcast included by a broadcaster in its broadcasting services.

47.6

In subsection  (5) —

                                    “ broadcaster ” has the meaning given in
section 37(2) of PPERA;
“ referendum campaign broadcast ” has the meaning given in section 127(2) of
PPERA.

47.7

The Secretary of State may by regulations amend this section so as to add,
modify or remove cases to which section 41 does not apply.

#### Enforcement

##### Offence of breaching section 41

48

48.1

Where any electronic material to which section 41 applies is published in
contravention of that section, the following persons are guilty of an offence—

48.1.a

the promoter of the material, and

48.1.b

any person on behalf of whom the material is being published (and who is not
the promoter).

48.2

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (1)  is liable—

48.2.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

48.2.b

on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding
level 5 on the standard scale.

48.3

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under subsection  (1)  to
prove—

48.3.a

that the contravention arose from circumstances beyond the person’s control,
and

48.3.b

that the person took all reasonable steps, and exercised all due diligence, to
ensure that the contravention would not arise.

48.4

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under subsection  (1)  to
prove that the person acted in accordance with guidance under section 54.

48.5

It is a defence for a person charged with an offence under  subsection (1)  in
relation to the republication of electronic material to prove that—

48.5.a

the electronic material had previously been published,

48.5.b

the person reasonably believed that when it was previously published—

48.5.b.i

section 41 applied to it, and

48.5.b.ii

it was published in compliance with that section, and

48.5.c

it was not materially altered when it was republished.

48.6

In subsection  (5) (c)  the reference to electronic material not being
materially altered includes a reference to the electronic material retaining—

48.6.a

the information within section 41(3), or

48.6.b

the access to such information,

as a result of which the person reasonably believed its previous publication
complied with section 41.

48.7

The court by or before which a person is convicted of an offence under
subsection  (1)  must notify the Commission of the person’s conviction and the
sentence imposed on the conviction as soon as is practicable.

48.8

This section is subject to  Schedule 11 , which provides for certain persons
who would otherwise be guilty of an offence under this section to be guilty of
an illegal practice.

48.9

See also section 49, which makes provision about the removal etc of electronic
material in the event of a conviction under this section.

##### Order to take down electronic material in breach of section 41

49

49.1

This section applies if, in respect of any electronic material, a person is
convicted of—

49.1.a

an offence under section 48 (1) , or

49.1.b

an illegal practice by virtue of  Schedule 11 .

49.2

The court by or before which the person is convicted of the offence or illegal
practice may order a person by whom the electronic material is published to
take the action specified in the order to remove the material, or to disable
access to it, before the end of the period specified in the order.

49.3

Where an order is made under subsection  (2) , the person to whom it applies
has the same right of appeal against it as if—

49.3.a

the person had committed the offence under section 48 (1)  or (as the case may
be) the illegal practice, and

49.3.b

the order were a sentence passed on the person for the offence or illegal
practice.

49.4

A person to whom an order under subsection  (2)  applies commits an offence
if, without reasonable excuse, the person fails to comply with the order.

49.5

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (4)  is liable—

49.5.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

49.5.b

on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding
level 5 on the standard scale.

49.6

The court by or before which a person is convicted of an offence under
subsection  (4)  must notify the Commission of the person’s conviction and the
sentence imposed on the conviction as soon as is practicable.

##### Enforcement by the Commission

50

50.1

Parts 1 to 4 and 6 of Schedule 19C to PPERA (civil sanctions) and the
Political Parties, Elections and Referendums (Civil Sanctions) Order 2010 (
S.I. 2010/2860 ) apply (subject to the following provisions of this section)
in relation to an offence to which this section applies as they apply in
relation to a prescribed offence under that Act.

50.2

This section applies to—

50.2.a

an offence under section 48 (1)  which relates to the publication of
electronic material which can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve a
purpose within—

50.2.a.i

section 43 (2)  (registered parties etc),

50.2.a.ii

section 43 (7)  (categories of elected office-holders), or

50.2.a.iii

section 43 (9)  (referendums) where the referendum in question is a referendum
to which Part 7 of PPERA applies and the electronic material is published
during the referendum period (within the meaning of that Part) for that
referendum, or

50.2.b

an offence under section 48 (1)  which relates to the publication of
electronic material—

50.2.b.i

which falls within section 44 (2) (b)  (referendums), or

50.2.b.ii

which can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve a purpose within
section 45 (2)  (registered parties etc).

50.3

In the application of paragraph 23 of Schedule 19C to PPERA (use of statements
made compulsorily) by virtue of this section, the reference in sub-paragraph
(1) of that paragraph to Schedule 19B to that Act is to be read as including a
reference to  Schedule 12  to this Act.

50.4

In the application of paragraph 13(1)(a) of Schedule 1 to the Political
Parties, Elections and Referendums (Civil Sanctions) Order 2010 ( S.I.
2010/2860 ) by virtue of this section, the reference to PPERA and that Order
is to be read as a reference to that Act and that Order as they are applied by
this section.

##### Notice to take down electronic material in breach of section 41

51

51.1

This section applies if—

51.1.a

the Commission imposes a fixed monetary penalty under paragraph 1 of Schedule
19C to PPERA on a person in relation to an offence under section 48 (1)  in
respect of any electronic material,

51.1.b

the Commission imposes a discretionary requirement under paragraph 5 of that
Schedule on a person in relation to such an offence,

51.1.c

the Commission serves a stop notice under paragraph 10 of that Schedule on a
person in relation to such an offence, or

51.1.d

the Commission accepts an undertaking under paragraph 15 of that Schedule from
a person in relation to such an offence.

51.2

The Commission may give a notice in writing to a person by whom the electronic
material is published requiring the person to take the action specified in the
notice to remove the material, or to disable access to it, before the end of
the period specified in the notice.

51.3

A person to whom a notice under subsection  (2)  has been given commits an
offence if, without reasonable excuse, the person fails to comply with the
notice. 

51.4

A person guilty of an offence under subsection  (3)  is liable—

51.4.a

on summary conviction in England and Wales, to a fine;

51.4.b

on summary conviction in Scotland or Northern Ireland, to a fine not exceeding
level 5 on the standard scale.

51.5

The court by or before which a person is convicted of an offence under
subsection  (3)  must notify the Commission of the person’s conviction and the
sentence imposed on the conviction as soon as is practicable.

51.6

This section is subject to section 52 (further provision about notices under
this section).

##### Further provision about notice under section 51

52

52.1

Before giving a notice under section 51 (2)  to a person the Commission must
give the person a notice in writing of its intention to do so.

52.2

The person may, within the period specified in the notice under subsection
(1) , make written representations to the Commission in relation to the
proposal to give the person a notice under section 51 (2) . 

52.3

The Commission may give the person a notice under section 51 (2)  only if—

52.3.a

the period for making representations has ended, and

52.3.b

having taken any representations made by the person into account, the
Commission is still of the view that it should give the person the notice
under section 51 (2) .

52.4

A notice under subsection  (1)  must include information as to—

52.4.a

the grounds for the proposal to give a notice to the person under section 51
(2) ,

52.4.b

the proposed effect of such a notice,

52.4.c

the right to make representations, and

52.4.d

the period within which representations may be made.

52.5

The period specified under subsection  (4) (d)  must not be less than 14 days
beginning with the day on which the notice is given.

52.6

A notice under section 51 (2)  must include information as to—

52.6.a

the grounds for serving the notice,

52.6.b

rights of appeal, and

52.6.c

the consequences of not complying with the notice.

52.7

The Commission may by notice in writing withdraw or vary a notice under
section 51 (2)  at any time.

52.8

A person to whom a notice under section 51 (2)  has been given may appeal
against the notice on the ground that—

52.8.a

the decision to give the notice was based on an error of fact,

52.8.b

the decision was wrong in law,

52.8.c

the decision was unreasonable, or

52.8.d

any action specified in the notice is unreasonable.

52.9

An appeal under subsection  (8)  is to—

52.9.a

in England and Wales, the county court,

52.9.b

in Scotland, a sheriff, or

52.9.c

in Northern Ireland, a county court.

52.10

On an appeal under subsection  (8)  the county court or the sheriff may—

52.10.a

withdraw, confirm or vary the notice, or

52.10.b

remit the decision whether to withdraw, confirm or vary the notice to the
Commission.

##### Supply of information

53

53.1

Schedule 12  makes provision about the supply of information for the purposes
of this Part.

53.2

Paragraphs 3 to 13 and 15 of Schedule 19B to PPERA (investigatory powers)
apply in relation to an offence within section 50 (2) (a)  or  (b)  as they
apply in relation to an offence under that Act.

#### Supplementary

##### Guidance

54

54.1

The Commission must prepare guidance about—

54.1.a

the operation of this Part, and

54.1.b

the exercise of functions by the Commission or a constable in relation to a
breach or suspected breach of this Part.

54.2

The Commission or a constable must have regard to guidance issued under this
section in exercising those functions.

54.3

Once the Commission has prepared draft guidance under this section, it must
submit it to the Secretary of State for approval by the Secretary of State.

54.4

The Secretary of State may approve draft guidance either without modifications
or with such modifications as the Secretary of State may determine.

54.5

Once the Secretary of State has approved draft guidance, the Secretary of
State must lay before each House of Parliament a copy of the draft, whether—

54.5.a

in its original form, or

54.5.b

in a form which incorporates any modifications determined under subsection
(4) .

54.6

If the draft guidance incorporates any such modifications, the Secretary of
State must at the same time lay before each House a statement of the Secretary
of State’s reasons for making them.

54.7

If, within the 40-day period, either House resolves not to approve the draft
guidance, the Secretary of State must take no further steps in relation to the
draft guidance.

54.8

Subsection  (7)  does not prevent new draft guidance from being laid before
Parliament.

54.9

If no resolution of the kind mentioned in subsection  (7)  is made within the
40-day period—

54.9.a

the Secretary of State must issue the guidance in the form of the draft laid
before Parliament,

54.9.b

the Commission must arrange for the guidance to be published in such manner as
it considers appropriate, and

54.9.c

the guidance comes into force on such day as the Secretary of State may by
regulations made by statutory instrument appoint.

54.10

The Commission—

54.10.a

may from time to time revise guidance under this section, and

54.10.b

must revise guidance under this section if directed to do so by the Secretary
of State.

54.11

References in this section (other than in subsection  (1) ) to guidance or
draft guidance include revised guidance or draft revised guidance.

54.12

In this section “ the 40-day period ”, in relation to draft guidance, means—

54.12.a

if the draft is laid before one House on a day later than the day on which it
is laid before the other House, the period of 40 days beginning with the later
of the two days, and

54.12.b

in any other case, the period of 40 days beginning with the day on which the
draft is laid before each House,

no account being taken of any period during which Parliament is dissolved or
prorogued or during which both Houses are adjourned for more than four days.

##### Information in Commission’s annual report

55

55.1

Each report by the Commission under paragraph 20 of Schedule 1 to PPERA must
contain information about—

55.1.a

the convictions reported to the Commission under section 48 (7) , 49 (6)  or
51 (5)  during the year in question,

55.1.b

the orders made under section 49 (orders to take down electronic material)
during that year,

55.1.c

the use made by the Commission of its powers under section 51 (notice to take
down electronic material) during that year, and

55.1.d

the use made by the Commission of its powers under  Schedule 12  (supply of
information) during that year.

55.2

The report must, in particular, specify—

55.2.a

the cases in which a notice was given under section 51 (2) ,

55.2.b

the cases in which a notice was given under paragraph  1  of  Schedule 12 ,
and

55.2.c

the cases in which an order under paragraph  2  or  3  of that Schedule was
applied for or made.

55.3

This section does not require the Commission to include in a report any
information that, in its opinion, it would be inappropriate to include on the
ground that to do so—

55.3.a

would or might be unlawful, or

55.3.b

might adversely affect any current investigation or proceedings.

##### Notices

56

56.1

A notice which may be given to a person under this Part by the Commission or a
constable may be given—

56.1.a

by delivering it to the person,

56.1.b

by leaving it at the person’s proper address,

56.1.c

by sending it by post to the person at that address, or

56.1.d

by sending it to the person by electronic means.

56.2

A notice to a body corporate may be given to an officer of that body.

56.3

A notice to a partnership may be given to a partner or a person who has the
control or management of the partnership business.

56.4

A notice to an unincorporated association (other than a partnership) may be
given to a member of the governing body of the association.

56.5

For the purposes of this section and of section 7 of the Interpretation Act
1978 (service of documents by post) in its application to this section, the
proper address of a person is the person’s last known address (whether of the
person’s residence or of a place where the person carries on business or is
employed) and also—

56.5.a

in the case of a body corporate or an officer of the body, the address of the
body’s registered or principal office in the United Kingdom;

56.5.b

in the case of a partnership, a partner or a person having the control or
management of the partnership business, the address of the principal office of
the partnership in the United Kingdom;

56.5.c

in the case of an unincorporated association (other than a partnership) or a
member of its governing body, the principal office of the association in the
United Kingdom.

56.6

If a person has specified an address in the United Kingdom, other than the
person’s proper address within the meaning of subsection (5), as the one at
which the person or someone on the person’s behalf will accept notices of the
same description as a notice under this Part, that address is also treated for
the purposes of this section and section 7 of the Interpretation Act 1978 as
the person’s proper address.

56.7

A notice sent to a person by electronic means is, unless the contrary is
proved, to be treated as having been given on the working day immediately
following the day on which it was sent.

56.8

In this section—

                                    “ officer ” in relation to a body
corporate, means a director, manager, secretary or other similar officer of
the body;
“ working day ” means a day other than a Saturday, a Sunday, Christmas Day,
Good Friday or a bank holiday under the Banking and Financial Dealings Act
1971 in any part of the United Kingdom.

##### Proceedings for an offence under this Part

57

57.1

Summary proceedings for an offence under this Part may, without prejudice to
any jurisdiction exercisable apart from this subsection, be taken against any
body, including an unincorporated association, at any place at which it has a
place of business, and against an individual at any place at which the
individual is for the time being.

57.2

Subsections  (3)  to  (7)  apply to—

57.2.a

an offence within section 50 (2) (a)  or  (b)  (offences in relation to which
the Commission may exercise enforcement functions), and

57.2.b

an offence under section 49 (4)  or 51 (3)  (order or notice to take down
electronic material).

57.3

Despite anything in section 127(1) of the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980, if the
offence is triable by a magistrates’ court in England and Wales, any
information relating to the offence may be so tried if it is laid at any time
within three years after the commission of the offence and within six months
after the relevant date.

57.4

Despite anything in section 136 of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995,
summary proceedings for the offence may be commenced in Scotland at any time
within three years after the commission of the offence and within six months
after the relevant date; and subsection (3) of that section applies for the
purposes of this subsection as it applies for the purposes of that section.

57.5

Despite anything in Article 19(1) of the Magistrates’ Courts (Northern
Ireland) Order 1981 ( S.I. 1981/1675 (N.I. 26)) , if the offence is triable by
a court of summary jurisdiction in Northern Ireland, a complaint relating to
the offence may be so tried if it is made at any time within three years after
the commission of the offence and within six months after the relevant date.

57.6

In subsections  (3)  to  (5)  “ the relevant date ” means the date on which
evidence sufficient in the opinion of the prosecutor to justify proceedings
comes to the prosecutor’s knowledge.

57.7

For the purposes of subsection  (6)  a certificate of any prosecutor as to the
date on which such evidence came to the prosecutor’s knowledge is conclusive
evidence of that fact.

57.8

Subsections  (9)  to  (15)  apply to an offence under this Part other than—

57.8.a

an offence within section 50 (2) (a)  or  (b) , or

57.8.b

an offence under section 49 (4)  or 51 (3) .

57.9

Despite anything in section 127(1) of the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980, if the
offence is triable by a magistrates’ court in England and Wales, any
information relating to the offence may be so tried if it is laid at any time
within one year after the commission of the offence.

57.10

Despite anything in section 136 of the Criminal Procedure (Scotland) Act 1995,
summary proceedings for the offence may be commenced in Scotland at any time
within one year after the commission of the offence; and subsection (3) of
that section applies for the purposes of this subsection as it applies for the
purposes of that section.

57.11

Despite anything in Article 19(1) of the Magistrates’ Courts (Northern
Ireland) Order 1981, if the offence is triable by a court of summary
jurisdiction in Northern Ireland, a complaint relating to the offence may be
so tried if it is made at any time within one year after the commission of the
offence.

57.12

A magistrates’ court in England and Wales may act under subsection  (13)  if
satisfied on an application by a constable or a Crown prosecutor—

57.12.a

that there are exceptional circumstances which justify the granting of the
application, and

57.12.b

that there has been no undue delay in the investigation of the offence to
which the application relates.

57.13

The magistrates’ court may extend the time within which proceedings must be
commenced in pursuance of subsection  (9)  to not more than two years after
the commission of the offence.

57.14

An application under subsection  (12)  must be made not more than one year
after the commission of the offence.

57.15

Any party to an application under subsection  (12)  who is aggrieved by the
refusal of the magistrates’ court to act under subsection  (13)  may appeal to
the Crown Court.

##### Offences committed by bodies corporate

58

58.1

Where an offence under this Part committed by a body corporate is proved to
have been committed with the consent or connivance of, or to be attributable
to any neglect on the part of—

58.1.a

a person who is a director, manager, secretary or other similar officer of the
body corporate, or

58.1.b

a person who was purporting to act in any such capacity,

that person, as well as the body corporate, is guilty of that offence and
liable to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

58.2

Where the affairs of a body corporate are managed by its members, subsection
(1)  applies in relation to the acts and defaults of a member in connection
with the member’s functions of management as if the member were a director of
the body corporate.

##### Offences committed by unincorporated associations etc

59

59.1

Proceedings for an offence alleged to have been committed under this Part by
an unincorporated association are to be brought against the association in its
own name (and not in that of any of its members) and, for the purposes of any
such proceedings, any rules of court relating to the service of documents have
effect as if the association were a corporation.

59.2

A fine imposed on an unincorporated association on its conviction of an
offence under this Part must be paid out of the funds of the association.

59.3

Schedule 3 to the Magistrates’ Courts Act 1980 (procedure on charge of offence
against a corporation) has effect in a case in which an unincorporated
association is charged in England or Wales with an offence under this Part in
the same way as it has effect in the case of a corporation so charged.

59.4

Schedule 4 to the Magistrates’ Courts (Northern Ireland) Order 1981 ( S.I.
1981/1675 (N.I. 26))  (procedure on charge of offence against a corporation)
has effect in a case in which an unincorporated association is charged in
Northern Ireland with an offence under this Part in the same way as it has
effect in the case of a corporation so charged.

59.5

Where a partnership is guilty of an offence under this Part and the offence is
proved to have been committed with the consent or connivance of, or to be
attributable to any neglect on the part of, any partner, the partner as well
as the partnership is guilty of that offence and liable to be proceeded
against and punished accordingly.

59.6

Where any other unincorporated association is guilty of an offence under this
Part and the offence is proved to have been committed with the consent or
connivance of, or to be attributable to any neglect on the part of—

59.6.a

any officer of the association, or

59.6.b

any member of the committee or other similar governing body of the
association,

the officer or member, as well as the association, is guilty of that offence
and liable to be proceeded against and punished accordingly.

##### Regulations under this Part

60

60.1

The Secretary of State may make regulations under this Part only—

60.1.a

where the regulations give effect to a recommendation of the Commission, or

60.1.b

after consultation with the Commission.

60.2

Regulations under this Part—

60.2.a

are to be made by statutory instrument;

60.2.b

may make consequential, incidental, supplementary, transitional, transitory or
saving provision.

60.3

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this Part may not be made
unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of each House of Parliament.

60.4

This section does not apply to regulations under section 54 (9) (c) .

##### Meaning of “the Commission”

61

In this Part “ the Commission ” means the Electoral Commission.

### General

#### Review of operation of Act

62

62.1

The Secretary of State must, within the review period—

62.1.a

prepare a report on the operation of this Act,

62.1.b

publish the report, and

62.1.c

lay a copy of the report before Parliament.

62.2

In subsection (1), “the review period” is the period—

62.2.a

beginning with the fourth anniversary of the day on which this Act is passed,
and

62.2.b

ending with the fifth anniversary of that day.

#### Power to amend references to subordinate legislation etc

63

63.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory instrument amend—

63.1.a

any provision of this Act, or

63.1.b

any provision inserted by this Act into another Act,

in consequence of the amendment or revocation of any subordinate legislation
which is for the time being referred to in the provision.

63.2

In subsection  (1) , “ subordinate legislation ” means—

63.2.a

subordinate legislation within the meaning of the Interpretation Act 1978, or

63.2.b

an instrument made under—

63.2.b.i

an Act of the Scottish Parliament,

63.2.b.ii

a Measure or Act of Senedd Cymru, or

63.2.b.iii

Northern Ireland legislation.

63.3

A statutory instrument containing regulations under subsection  (1)  may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before, and approved by
a resolution of, each House of Parliament.

#### Financial provisions

64

64.1

There is to be paid out of money provided by Parliament—

64.1.a

any expenditure incurred by a Minister of the Crown under or by virtue of this
Act, and

64.1.b

any increase attributable to this Act in the sums payable under any other Act
out of money so provided.

64.2

There is to be paid out of the Consolidated Fund any increase attributable to
this Act in the sums payable under any other Act out of that Fund.

64.3

There is to be paid into the Consolidated Fund any increase attributable to
this Act in the sums payable into that Fund under any other Act.

#### Interpretation etc

65

In this Act—

“ PPERA ” means the Political Parties, Elections and Referendums Act 2000; “
RPA 1983 ” means the Representation of the People Act 1983.

66.2.b

paragraphs  3 , 11,  17 , 26,  35 ,  37  and  39  of  Schedule 1 , and section
1 so far as relating to those provisions;

66.2.b.ii

paragraphs  9  and  11  of  Schedule 4 , and section 6 so far as relating to
those paragraphs;

66.2.b.iii

paragraphs  32 ,  33 ,  47  and  48  of  Schedule 6 , and section 12 so far as
relating to those paragraphs;

66.2.c

amended, repealed or revoked, except where contained in a provision for which
a different extent is provided by this subsection.

#### Commencement

67

67.1

Subject to  subsection (3) , the provisions of this Act come into force on
such day as the Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory
instrument appoint.

67.2

Regulations under  subsection (1)  may appoint different days for different
purposes or areas.

67.3

This Part comes into force on the day on which this Act is passed.

67.4

The Secretary of State may by regulations made by statutory instrument make
transitional, transitory or saving provision in connection with the coming
into force of any provision of this Act.

67.5

Regulations under  subsection (4)  may make different provision for different
purposes or areas.

#### Short title

68

This Act may be cited as the Elections Act 2022.

## Schedules

Voter identification

Section 1

##### Amendments of RPA 1983

1

RPA 1983 is amended as follows.

2

After section 13BC insert—

######## Electoral identity document: Great Britain

2.13BD

2.13BD.1

An application for an electoral identity document may be made by a person who—

2.13BD.1.a

is or has applied to be registered in a register of parliamentary electors in
Great Britain or a register of local government electors in England, or

2.13BD.1.b

is or has applied to be registered in a register of local government electors
in Wales and—

2.13BD.1.b.i

is entitled to vote or, as the case may be, will on being registered be
entitled to vote, at an election of a police and crime commissioner for a
police area in Wales (see section 52(1A) of the Police Reform and Social
Responsibility Act 2011), or

2.13BD.1.b.ii

will be entitled to vote or, as the case may be, will on being registered be
entitled to vote, at such an election on attaining the age of 18.

2.13BD.2

An application must be made to a registration officer who maintains a register
referred to in subsection (1) in which the applicant is or has applied to be
registered.

2.13BD.3

A registration officer must, in accordance with regulations, determine an
application made to the registration officer.

2.13BD.4

Regulations may make provision—

2.13BD.4.a

about the timing of an application for an electoral identity document;

2.13BD.4.b

about the issuing or collection of an electoral identity document.

2.13BD.5

Regulations under  subsection (4) (a)  may in particular provide for an
application to be disregarded for the purposes of a particular election where
the application is received after a deadline specified by reference to the
date of that election.

2.13BD.6

The provision that may be made by virtue of  subsection (4) (b)  includes
provision amending the parliamentary elections rules in connection with the
collection of an electoral identity document from a polling station.

2.13BD.7

No charge may be made for the issue of an electoral identity document.

2.13BD.8

Regulations must require an electoral identity document issued to a person—

2.13BD.8.a

to state the person’s full name, and

2.13BD.8.b

to contain a photograph of the person.

2.13BD.9

Regulations may require an electoral identity document to include other
information.

2.13BD.10

Regulations may make provision about—

2.13BD.10.a

the form of an electoral identity document (including provision for the
document to be issued in different forms in different circumstances), and

2.13BD.10.b

the period for which an electoral identity document issued in a particular
form is to be valid.

2.13BD.11

Regulations under subsection (9) or (10)(a) may confer functions on the
Electoral Commission (for example, the Commission may be required to design an
electoral identity document).

######## Anonymous elector’s document: Great Britain

2.13BE

2.13BE.1

An application for an anonymous elector’s document may be made by a person
who—

2.13BE.1.a

has or has applied for an anonymous entry in a register of parliamentary
electors in Great Britain or a register of local government electors in
England, or

2.13BE.1.b

has or has applied for an anonymous entry in a register of local government
electors in Wales and—

2.13BE.1.b.i

is entitled to vote or, as the case may be, will on having an anonymous entry
in the register be entitled to vote, at an election of a police and crime
commissioner for a police area in Wales (see section 52(1A) of the Police
Reform and Social Responsibility Act 2011), or

2.13BE.1.b.ii

will be entitled to vote or, as the case may be, will on having an anonymous
entry in the register be entitled to vote, at such an election on attaining
the age of 18.

2.13BE.2

An application must be made to a registration officer who maintains a register
referred to in subsection (1) in which the applicant has or has applied for an
anonymous entry.

2.13BE.3

A registration officer must, in accordance with regulations, determine an
application made to the registration officer.

2.13BE.4

Regulations may make provision—

2.13BE.4.a

about the timing of an application for an anonymous elector’s document;

2.13BE.4.b

about the issuing or collection of an anonymous elector’s document.

2.13BE.5

Regulations under subsection  (4) (a)  may in particular provide for an
application to be disregarded for the purposes of a particular election where
the application is received after a deadline specified by reference to the
date of that election.

2.13BE.6

The provision that may be made by virtue of subsection  (4) (b)  includes
provision amending the parliamentary elections rules in connection with the
collection of an anonymous elector’s document from a polling station.

2.13BE.7

No charge may be made for the issue of an anonymous elector’s document.

2.13BE.8

Regulations must require an anonymous elector’s document issued to a person—

2.13BE.8.a

to state the person’s electoral number, and

2.13BE.8.b

to contain a photograph of the person.

2.13BE.9

Regulations may require an anonymous elector’s document to include other
information.

2.13BE.10

Regulations may make provision about—

2.13BE.10.a

the form of an anonymous elector’s document (including provision for the
document to be issued in different forms in different circumstances), and

2.13BE.10.b

the period for which an anonymous elector’s document issued in a particular
form is to be valid.

2.13BE.11

Regulations under subsection (9) or (10)(a) may confer functions on the
Electoral Commission (for example, the Commission may be required to design an
anonymous elector’s document).

2.13BE.12

Regulations—

2.13BE.12.a

may authorise or require a registration officer to remind a person who has an
anonymous entry in a register maintained by the officer of the need to obtain
an anonymous elector’s document in order to be able to vote in person;

2.13BE.12.b

may require a registration officer, in prescribed circumstances, to replace an
anonymous elector’s document issued to a person with a new anonymous elector’s
document issued by the officer.

After section 59 (supplemental provisions as to members of forces and service

######## Reports on voter identification requirements in Great Britain

7.59A

7.59A.1

The Secretary of State must prepare and publish reports on the effect of the
voter identification requirements on applications made under rule 37(1),
38(1), 39(1) or 40(1) of the parliamentary elections rules.

7.59A.2

The duty under subsection (1) applies in respect of each of the first two
parliamentary general elections that are held after the day on which
paragraph 7  of  Schedule 1  to the Elections Act 2022 comes into force.

7.59A.3

Subsection (4) applies where requirements corresponding to the voter
identification requirements (“the corresponding requirements”) have effect in
relation to local government elections in England by virtue of rules made
under section 36.

7.59A.4

The Secretary of State must prepare and publish reports on the effect of the
corresponding requirements on applications made under the provisions of rules
made under section 36 corresponding to rules 37(1), 38(1), 39(1) and 40(1) of
the parliamentary elections rules.

7.59A.5

The duty under subsection (4) applies in respect of the first ordinary
elections of councillors for local government areas in England that—

7.59A.5.a

are held on an ordinary day of election (as determined under section 37) after
the day on which the corresponding requirements come into force, and

7.59A.5.b

are not combined with a parliamentary general election.

7.59A.6

In preparing a report under this section, the Secretary of State must in
particular take into account—

7.59A.6.a

in the case of a report under subsection (1), information provided to the
Secretary of State under rule 40B of the parliamentary elections rules
(collection and disclosure of information relating to applications under rules
37 to 40);

7.59A.6.b

in the case of a report under subsection (4), information provided to the
Secretary of State under any provision of rules made under section 36
corresponding to rule 40B of the parliamentary elections rules.

7.59A.7

In this section, “ the voter identification requirements ” means paragraphs
(1A)  to  (1T)  of rule 37 of the parliamentary elections rules (voting
procedure) as it extends to England and Wales and to Scotland (including those
paragraphs as applied by rule 38, 39 or 40 of those rules).
