11

After rule 19A insert—

######## Date of birth lists for polling stations in Northern Ireland

11.19B

11.19B.1

The Chief Electoral Officer for Northern Ireland must prepare the following
lists for each polling station—

11.19B.1.a

a list setting out, in relation to each elector allotted to the polling
station, the elector’s date of birth as supplied pursuant to section
10(4A)(b), 10A(1A)(b) or 13A(2A)(b);

11.19B.1.b

a list setting out, in relation to each person appointed to vote as proxy for
an elector allotted to the polling station, the person’s date of birth as
supplied pursuant to a relevant provision.

11.19B.2

For the purposes of paragraph  (1) (b) , “ relevant provision ” means—

11.19B.2.a

where the person is or will be registered in a register of parliamentary
electors in Northern Ireland, section 10(4A)(b), 10A(1A)(b) or 13A(2A)(b), and

11.19B.2.b

where the person is or will be registered in a register of parliamentary
electors in Great Britain and does not also fall within sub-paragraph (a),
section 8(7A) of the Representation of the People Act 1985.

11.19B.3

A list prepared under paragraph  (1)  must include sufficient information for
the purposes of enabling the presiding officer or a clerk at the polling
station to make a decision under rule 37(1B)(a)(ii) (decision whether
specified document raises doubt as to voter’s apparent age).

11.19B.4

A person to whom paragraph  (5)  applies must not, otherwise than in
accordance with these rules (including regulations under paragraph  (6) )—

11.19B.4.a

permit a list prepared under paragraph  (1)  for a polling station to be
inspected;

11.19B.4.b

supply to any person a copy of a list prepared under paragraph  (1)  for a
polling station or information contained in such a list;

11.19B.4.c

make use of information contained in a list prepared under paragraph  (1) .

11.19B.5

This paragraph applies to—

11.19B.5.a

the Chief Electoral Officer for Northern Ireland;

11.19B.5.b

a person to whom functions are delegated by the Chief Electoral Officer;

11.19B.5.c

the presiding officer of the polling station;

11.19B.5.d

a clerk or other officer appointed to work at the polling station.

11.19B.6

Regulations may make provision—

11.19B.6.a

enabling the inspection of a list prepared under paragraph  (1)  by prescribed
persons;

11.19B.6.b

authorising or requiring prescribed persons to supply a copy of a list
prepared under paragraph  (1)  to such persons as may be prescribed;

11.19B.6.c

for the payment of a fee in respect of the inspection of a list or the supply
of a copy of a list.

11.19B.7

Regulations under paragraph  (6) (a)  or  (b)  may impose conditions in
relation to—

11.19B.7.a

the inspection of a list;

11.19B.7.b

the supply of a copy of a list;

11.19B.7.c

the purposes for which information contained in a list that is inspected or
supplied in pursuance of the regulations may be used.

11.19B.8

The conditions that may be imposed by virtue of paragraph  (7) (b)  include
conditions relating to the extent to which a person to whom a copy of a list
has been supplied may—

11.19B.8.a

supply the copy to any other person,

11.19B.8.b

disclose to any other person information contained in the copy, or

11.19B.8.c

use any such information for a purpose other than that for which the copy was
supplied to the person.

11.19B.9

Regulations under paragraph  (6)  may also impose, in respect of persons to
whom a copy of a list has been supplied or information has been disclosed by
virtue of paragraph  (8) , conditions corresponding to those mentioned in
paragraph  (8) .

16.1

Rule 35 (questions to be put to voters) is amended as follows.

16.2

In the table following paragraph (1), in the column headed “Questions”, in

anonymous entry), entry 5 (postal voters) and entry 6 (proxy postal voters),
before question (a) insert—

16.2.za

At an election held in England and Wales or Scotland, “What is your name?”

16.2.zb

At an election held in England and Wales or Scotland, “What is your address?”

16.3

Before paragraph (3) insert—

16.3.2B

In the case of an election held in England and Wales or Scotland, where a
clerk—

16.3.2B.a

gives a person the required information (see paragraph (5)),

16.3.2B.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person, and

16.3.2B.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the clerk must refer the matter to the presiding officer, who must put the
question to the person again.

16.4

For paragraph (3) substitute—

16.4.3

Where the presiding officer—

16.4.3.a

gives a person the required information,

16.4.3.b

puts a question specified in paragraph (1) to the person (whether or not, in
the case of an election held in England and Wales or Scotland, following a
referral under paragraph (2B)), and

16.4.3.c

decides that the person has failed to answer the question satisfactorily,

the officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to the person.

In the case of an election held in England and Wales or Scotland, see rule
40ZB (procedure where ballot paper is refused under this paragraph).

16.4.3A

For the purposes of this rule, a person answers the question “What is your
name?” or “What is your address?” satisfactorily if—

16.4.3A.a

where one of those questions is put, the answer matches a name or address (as
the case may be) in the register of parliamentary electors;

16.4.3A.b

where both those questions are put, the answers match a name and address in
that register that relate to the same person.

16.4.3B

In the case of an elector in respect of whom a notice has been issued under
section 13B(3B) or (3D), the references to the register in paragraph (3A)
above are to be read as references to the notice issued under section 13B(3B)
or (3D).

paragraph, an inquiry relating to the production of identification by a voter
is not to be regarded as an inquiry as to the right of the person to vote)” .

16.6.5

For the purposes of this rule, a person to whom any question is to be put is
given “the required information” if the person is first informed that—

16.6.5.a

a ballot paper will be refused if the person fails to answer each question
satisfactorily, and

16.6.5.b

giving false information may be an offence.

18

18.1

Rule 37 (voting procedure), as it extends to England and Wales and to
Scotland, is amended as follows.

18.2

For the heading substitute  “Voting procedure and voter identification
requirements: Great Britain” .

18.3

In paragraph (1)—

18.3.a

for “A” substitute  “Subject to rule 35(3) and to paragraphs  (1A)  to  (1P) ,
a” , and

18.3.b

omit sub-paragraph (a).

18.4

After paragraph (1) insert—

18.4.1A

A ballot paper must not be delivered to a voter unless the voter produces a
specified document to the presiding officer or a clerk.

18.4.1B

The presiding officer or clerk must arrange for the voter to produce any
document in a private area of the polling station if the voter so requests,
and, in such a case, must ensure that no other persons witness the production
except as permitted by the voter.

18.4.1C

Paragraph  (1D)  applies in relation to a voter where—

18.4.1C.a

the voter produces a specified document to a clerk and the clerk decides that
the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the elector
or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

18.4.1C.b

the voter produces a document to a clerk that the clerk reasonably suspects to
be a forged document (see paragraph  (1P) ).

18.4.1D

Where this paragraph applies, the clerk must refer the matter and produce the
document to the presiding officer, who must proceed as if the voter had
produced the document to the presiding officer in the first place.

18.4.1E

The presiding officer must refuse to deliver a ballot paper to a voter where—

18.4.1E.a

the voter produces a specified document to the officer and the officer decides
that the document raises a reasonable doubt as to whether the voter is the
elector or proxy that the voter claims to be, or

18.4.1E.b

the voter produces a document to the officer that the officer reasonably
suspects to be a forged document.

See rule 40ZB (procedure where ballot paper is refused under this paragraph).

18.4.1F

But there is an exception from paragraph  (1E)  for cases within sub-paragraph
(a) of that paragraph where—

18.4.1F.a

a discrepancy between the name of the holder of a specified document and the
name of the elector or proxy that the voter claims to be is resolved to the
presiding officer’s satisfaction at the time of the application by the voter
producing further proof of identity, and

18.4.1F.b

the presiding officer has no other reason (arising from any document produced
by the voter) to doubt that the voter is the elector or proxy that the voter
claims to be.

18.4.1G

The refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under paragraph  (1E)  does
not prevent the voter making a further application under paragraph (1), and
paragraphs  (1A)  to  (1F)  apply on any further application.

18.4.1H

In this rule a “specified document”, except in the case of a voter with an
anonymous entry in the register of electors (as to which see paragraph  (1K)
), means any of the following documents (in whatever form issued to the
holder) that contain a photograph of the holder—

18.4.1H.a

a United Kingdom passport (see paragraph  (1I) );

18.4.1H.b

a passport issued by an EEA state or a Commonwealth country;

18.4.1H.c

a licence to drive a motor vehicle granted under—

18.4.1H.c.i

Part 3 of the Road Traffic Act 1988, or

18.4.1H.c.ii

the Road Traffic (Northern Ireland) Order 1981 ( SI 1981/154 (N.I. 1)) ;

18.4.1H.d

a driving licence issued by any of the Channel Islands, the Isle of Man or an
EEA state;

18.4.1H.e

a biometric immigration document issued in accordance with regulations under
section 5 of the UK Borders Act 2007;

18.4.1H.f

an identity card bearing the Proof of Age Standards Scheme hologram (a PASS
card);

18.4.1H.g

a Ministry of Defence Form 90 (Defence Identity Card);

18.4.1H.h

a relevant concessionary travel pass (see paragraph  (1J) );

18.4.1H.i

a badge of a form prescribed under section 21 of the Chronically Sick and
Disabled Persons Act 1970 or section 14 of the Chronically Sick and Disabled
Persons (Northern Ireland) Act 1978 (blue badge scheme);

18.4.1H.j

an electoral identity document issued under  section 13BD  (electoral identity
document: Great Britain);

18.4.1H.k

an electoral identity card issued under section 13C (electoral identity card:
Northern Ireland);

18.4.1H.l

a national identity card issued by an EEA state.

18.4.1I

In paragraph  (1H) (a)  “ United Kingdom passport ” means a passport issued
by—

18.4.1I.a

the Government of the United Kingdom,

18.4.1I.b

the Lieutenant-Governor of any of the Channel Islands or the Isle of Man, or

18.4.1I.c

the Government of any British overseas territory.

18.4.1J

In paragraph (1H)(h), “ relevant concessionary travel pass ” means a
concessionary travel pass listed in the second column of the following table—

passes funded by the Government of the United Kingdom an Older Person’s Bus
Pass a Disabled Person’s Bus Pass an Oyster 60+ card a Freedom Pass passes
funded by the Scottish Government the National Entitlement Card passes funded
by the Welsh Government a 60 and Over Welsh Concessionary Travel Card a
Disabled Person’s Welsh Concessionary Travel Card passes issued under the
Northern Ireland Concessionary Fares Scheme a Senior SmartPass a Registered
Blind SmartPass or Blind Person’s SmartPass a War Disablement SmartPass or War
Disabled SmartPass a 60+ SmartPass a Half Fare SmartPass

18.4.1K

In this rule a “specified document”, in the case of a voter who has an
anonymous entry in the register of electors, means an anonymous elector’s
document issued to the voter under section 13BE which—

18.4.1K.a

was issued by an appropriate registration officer, and

18.4.1K.b

contains the voter’s electoral number.

18.4.1L

For the purposes of paragraph  (1K) —

“ appropriate registration officer ” means— the registration officer for the
constituency in which the election is being held, or where the election is
being held in a constituency for which there is more than one registration
officer, any of those officers; a voter’s “ electoral number ” is the number—
allocated to the voter as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or
where an entry relating to the voter is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D), as stated in the copy of that
notice.

18.4.1M

A reference in this rule to a document that is a specified document is a
reference to the document regardless of any expiry date relating to it
(subject to paragraph  (1N) ).

18.4.1N

Paragraph  (1M)  does not apply to a document which—

18.4.1N.a

is referred to in paragraph (1H)(j) or  (1K) , and

18.4.1N.b

in accordance with regulations made by virtue of section 13BD or 13BE (as the
case may be), is issued for use only at a particular poll or at particular
polls being held on the same day.

18.4.1P

In this rule a “ forged document ” means a false document made to resemble a
specified document.

18.4.1Q

Regulations may make provisions varying paragraph (1H),  (1I)  or  (1J)  by—

18.4.1Q.a

adding a reference to a document to any of those paragraphs,

18.4.1Q.b

removing a reference to a document from any of those paragraphs (other than
the document referred to in paragraph (1H)(j)), or

18.4.1Q.c

varying any description of document referred to in any of those paragraphs.

18.4.1R

The power to make provision by virtue of paragraph  (1Q) (b)  is exercisable
only on, and in accordance with, a recommendation of the Electoral Commission.

18.4.1S

No person other than the presiding officer or a clerk may inspect a document
produced as proof of a voter’s identity, except as permitted by the voter.

18.4.1T

References in this rule to producing a document are to producing it for
inspection.

18.5

In paragraph (2), omit the words from “and only” to the end.

18.6

In paragraph (3), omit sub-paragraph (a).

22

After rule 40ZA insert—

######## Refusal to deliver ballot paper: Great Britain

22.40ZB

22.40ZB.1

This rule applies in relation to an election held in England and Wales or
Scotland.

22.40ZB.2

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as an elector, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

22.40ZB.2.a

the voter’s electoral number, and

22.40ZB.2.b

against that number, the reason for the refusal.

22.40ZB.3

Where a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter who
applied for one as a proxy, the officer or a clerk must enter on the ballot
paper refusal list—

22.40ZB.3.a

the name and address of the voter, and

22.40ZB.3.b

against those details, the reason for the refusal.

22.40ZB.4

Paragraphs (5) and (6) apply where—

22.40ZB.4.a

a presiding officer refuses to deliver a ballot paper to a voter under rule 37
(1E) , and

22.40ZB.4.b

the voter makes a further application under rule 37(1).

22.40ZB.5

If a ballot paper is delivered to the voter following a further application,
the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper
refusal list.

22.40ZB.6

If the presiding officer again refuses to deliver a ballot paper to the voter,
the presiding officer or a clerk must note that fact on the ballot paper
refusal list.

22.40ZB.7

Entries required by this rule to be made on the ballot paper refusal list must
be made as soon as practicable after delivery of a ballot paper to a voter is
refused (or, in the case mentioned in paragraph (5), as soon as practicable
after the delivery of a ballot paper to a voter).

22.40ZB.8

For the purposes of paragraph (2)(a), a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

22.40ZB.8.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

22.40ZB.8.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D), as stated in the copy of that
notice.

22.40ZB.9

Subject to rule 37 (1G)  and paragraph (10), a refusal to deliver a ballot
paper to a voter is final and may not be questioned in any proceeding
whatsoever.

22.40ZB.10

A refusal to deliver a ballot paper to a voter is subject to review on an
election petition.

22.40ZB.11

In this rule—

22.40ZB.11.a

except in paragraph (4)(a), any reference to the refusal to deliver a ballot
paper (however expressed) is to the refusal to do so under rule 35(3) or 37
(1E) , and

22.40ZB.11.b

any reference to paragraph  (1E)  or  (1G)  of rule 37 includes a reference to
that paragraph as applied by rule 38, 39 or 40.

23

In rule 40A—

23.a

for the heading substitute  “Refusal to deliver ballot paper: Northern
Ireland” ;

23.b

in paragraph (2), after “that” insert  “and to rule 37 (1DB) ” .

24

After rule 40A insert—

######## Collection and disclosure of information relating to applications made under rules 37 to 40

24.40B

24.40B.1

This rule applies in relation to an election held in England and Wales or
Scotland if—

24.40B.1.a

regulations provide that this rule applies in relation to the election, or

24.40B.1.b

the election is within a description of elections in relation to which
regulations provide that this rule applies.

24.40B.2

A presiding officer must—

24.40B.2.a

collect prescribed information relating to applications made under rules
37(1), 38(1), 39(1) and 40(1), and

24.40B.2.b

provide the prescribed information to the returning officer as soon as
practicable after the close of the poll.

24.40B.3

Where the prescribed information relates to an election held in England and
Wales—

24.40B.3.a

the returning officer must forward the information to the relevant
registration officer, and

24.40B.3.b

the relevant registration officer must, as soon as reasonably practicable
after receiving the information, deal with it as required by paragraph  (5) .

24.40B.4

Where the prescribed information relates to an election held in Scotland, the
returning officer must deal with it as required by paragraph  (5) .

24.40B.5

The relevant registration officer or (as the case may be) the returning
officer must—

24.40B.5.a

anonymise the prescribed information by removing from it all names and
electoral numbers of the people to whom the information relates, and

24.40B.5.b

collate the information in the prescribed manner.

The information as anonymised and collated in accordance with this paragraph
is referred to in the rest of this rule as “the paragraph  (5)  information”.

24.40B.6

The relevant registration officer or (as the case may be) the returning
officer must provide the paragraph  (5)  information—

24.40B.6.a

to the Secretary of State, as soon as reasonably practicable after taking the
steps required by paragraph  (5) , and

24.40B.6.b

where they request the information, to the Electoral Commission.

24.40B.7

The relevant registration officer or (as the case may be) the returning
officer must not disclose the paragraph  (5)  information otherwise than in
accordance with paragraph  (6) .

24.40B.8

The relevant registration officer or (as the case may be) the returning
officer must retain the information anonymised in accordance with paragraph
(5) (a)  for at least 10 years.

24.40B.9

For the purposes of paragraph  (5) (a) , a person’s “electoral number” is the
number—

24.40B.9.a

allocated to the person as stated in the copy of the register of electors, or

24.40B.9.b

where an entry relating to the person is added to the register in pursuance of
a notice issued under section 13B(3B) or (3D), as stated in the copy of that
notice.

24.40B.10

Except as provided by paragraph  (11) , a disclosure of information under this
rule does not breach—

24.40B.10.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the presiding officer, the returning
officer or a registration officer, or

24.40B.10.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

24.40B.11

Nothing in this rule authorises the making of a disclosure that contravenes
the data protection legislation (but in determining whether a disclosure would
do so, the duties imposed by paragraphs  (2)  and  (3)  are to be taken into
account).

24.40B.12

In this rule—

24.40B.12.a

“ the data protection legislation ” has the same meaning as in the Data
Protection Act 2018 (see section 3(9) of that Act);

24.40B.12.b

references to the relevant registration officer are to—

24.40B.12.b.i

the registration officer of the local authority in whose area the constituency
is situated, or

24.40B.12.b.ii

if the constituency comprises any part of the area of more than one local
authority, the registration officer of the local authority in whose area the
greater or greatest (as the case may be) number of electors is registered.

##### Power to remove signature requirements

12

12.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations—

12.1.a

amend Schedule 4 to the Representation of the People Act 2000 (absent voting
in Great Britain) by removing any requirement for an application under
paragraph 3, 4 or 7 of that Schedule, other than an excluded application, to
contain the applicant’s signature;

12.1.b

amend section 6 or 7 of the Representation of the People Act 1985 (absent
voting at parliamentary elections in Northern Ireland) by removing any
requirement for an application under either of those sections to contain the
applicant’s signature.

12.2

In sub-paragraph (1), “ excluded application ” means an application in
relation to a local government election, or local government elections, in
Scotland or Wales.

12.3

Regulations under sub-paragraph (1) may make—

12.3.a

different provision for different purposes;

12.3.b

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional, transitory or saving
provision.

12.4

The consequential provision that may be made by virtue of sub-paragraph (3)(b)
includes provision amending any provision made by the Representation of the
People Acts.

12.5

Regulations under sub-paragraph (1) are to be made by statutory instrument.

12.6

A statutory instrument containing regulations under sub-paragraph (1) may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

##### Power to make provision about unique reference numbers: elections in Northern Ireland

13

13.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision about the issuing or
use of unique reference numbers in connection with—

13.1.a

applications for registration in a register of parliamentary electors, or a
register of local electors, in Northern Ireland;

13.1.b

applications to vote by post or proxy at parliamentary or local elections in
Northern Ireland;

13.1.c

a canvass under section 10 of RPA 1983 (maintenance of registers: duty to
conduct canvass in Northern Ireland).

13.2

Regulations under sub-paragraph (1) may in particular make provision—

13.2.a

amending or repealing section 10B of RPA 1983 or any other provision made by
the Representation of the People Acts about unique reference numbers allocated
under that section;

13.2.b

amending or repealing any provision made by the Elected Authorities (Northern
Ireland) Act 1989 about such unique reference numbers;

13.2.c

changing how unique reference numbers are referred to in any provision made by
the Representation of the People Acts or the Elected Authorities (Northern
Ireland) Act 1989.

13.3

Regulations under sub-paragraph (1) may make—

13.3.a

different provision for different purposes;

13.3.b

consequential, supplementary, incidental, transitional, transitory or saving
provision.

13.4

The consequential provision that may be made by virtue of sub-paragraph (3)(b)
includes provision amending any provision made by the Representation of the
People Acts or the Elected Authorities (Northern Ireland) Act 1989.

13.5

Regulations under sub-paragraph (1) are to be made by statutory instrument.

13.6

A statutory instrument containing regulations under sub-paragraph (1) may not
be made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by
a resolution of each House of Parliament.

Restriction of period for which person can apply for postal vote

Section 3

##### Representation of the People Act 2000

1

Schedule 4 to the Representation of the People Act 2000 (absent voting in
Great Britain) is amended as follows.

2

2.1

Paragraph 3 (absent vote at elections for definite or indefinite period) is
amended as follows.

2.2

In sub-paragraph (1)—

2.2.a

in the opening words, omit “(whether for an indefinite period or for a
particular period specified in his application)”;

2.2.b

in paragraph (b), after “requirements” insert  “and, in the case of an
application to vote by post at local government elections in Scotland or Wales
for a particular period, specifies the period.”

2.3

After sub-paragraph (1) insert—

2.3.1A

Any grant of an application under sub-paragraph (1) to vote by post at
parliamentary elections, or at local government elections in England, is to be
for—

2.3.1A.a

the period ending with the third 31 January following the date on which the
application is granted, or

2.3.1A.b

any shorter period specified in the application.

2.3.1B

But where the person is or will be registered in the register of parliamentary
electors in pursuance of an overseas elector’s declaration,  sub-paragraph
(1A)  does not apply and instead any grant of an application to vote by post
at parliamentary elections is to be for—

2.3.1B.a

the period ending with the 1 November until which, by virtue of  section 1D
(1) (a)  or  (3) (a)  of the Representation of the People Act 1985, the person
is entitled to remain registered in that register, or

##### Transitional provision

4

4.1

This paragraph applies where, immediately before the day specified for the
purposes of  this paragraph  (“the specified day”), a person has a relevant
postal vote entitlement lasting for—

4.1.a

an indefinite period, or

4.1.b

a period that would expire after the end of 3 years beginning with the
specified day.

4.2

A “ relevant postal vote entitlement ” means an entitlement, resulting from
the grant of a pre-commencement application, to vote by post (whether as
elector or proxy) at parliamentary elections in England and Wales or Scotland
or at local government elections in England (or both).

4.3

The person’s relevant postal vote entitlement ends on the applicable 31
January (unless it ends sooner).

4.4

“ The applicable 31 January ” means—

4.4.a

the third 31 January following the specified day, or

4.4.b

if sooner, the signature refresh date.

4.5

“ The signature refresh date ” means the 31 January by which the registration
officer would be required to send the person a regulation 60A notice (assuming
no change in the person’s entitlement or entitlements to vote by post or by
proxy after the specified day, and disregarding  sub-paragraph (9) ).

4.6

As soon as practicable after the specified day, the registration officer must
alter the record kept under paragraph 3(4) or 7(6) of Schedule 4 to RPA 2000
(as the case may be) so as to reflect any change resulting from  sub-paragraph
(3)  in the period for which the person’s relevant postal vote entitlement
lasts.

4.7

The registration officer must, before the applicable 31 January, send the
person—

4.7.a

a notice informing the person of the date on which the person’s relevant
postal vote entitlement is to end, and

4.7.b

information about how to make a fresh application to vote by post (as elector
or, as the case may be, as proxy).

4.8

Sub-paragraph (9)  applies where, as a result of  sub-paragraph (3) , a
person’s relevant postal vote entitlement is to end on the signature refresh
date.

4.9

Any requirement to send the person a regulation 60A notice by the signature
refresh date does not apply, unless—

4.9.a

the person has an entitlement (or entitlements) due to continue beyond that
date—

4.9.a.i

to vote by post (whether as elector or proxy) at local government elections in
Scotland or Wales,

4.9.a.ii

to vote by proxy at parliamentary elections in England and Wales or Scotland
or at local government elections in England (or both), or

4.9.a.iii

to vote by proxy at local government elections in Scotland or Wales, and

4.9.b

regulation 60A applies in relation to that entitlement (or those
entitlements).

4.10

Expressions used in  this paragraph  and in Schedule 4 to RPA 2000 have the
same meaning as in that Schedule.

4.11

This paragraph does not apply in relation to a person who is registered in a
register of parliamentary electors in pursuance of an overseas elector’s
declaration made at any time before the day on which section 14 comes fully
into force (see instead  Part 2  of  Schedule 7 ).

4.12

In  this paragraph —

“ pre-commencement application ” means an application made under paragraph
3(1) or 7(4)(a) of Schedule 4 to RPA 2000 before the specified day; “ register
of parliamentary electors ” means a register of parliamentary electors
maintained under section 9 of RPA 1983; “ regulation 60A ” means regulation
60A (requirement to provide fresh signatures) of the Representation of the
People (England and Wales) Regulations 2001 ( S.I. 2001/341 ) or the
Representation of the People (Scotland) Regulations 2001 ( S.I. 2001/497) (S.
2) ; “ regulation 60A notice ” means a notice under regulation 60A; “ RPA 2000
” means the Representation of the People Act 2000; “ specified ” means
specified by the Secretary of State in regulations made by statutory
instrument.

Proxy voting: limits and transitional provision

Section 6

##### Representation of the People Act 1983

1

RPA 1983 is amended as follows.

2

2.1

Section 61 (other voting offences) is amended as follows.

2.2

After subsection (1) insert—

2.2.1A

A person (“ P ”) is guilty of an offence if P applies for the appointment of a
proxy to vote for P—

2.2.1A.a

at a parliamentary election, where P knows that the person to be appointed is
already appointed as proxy to vote at that election, or at parliamentary
elections, for four or more other electors;

2.2.1A.b

at a parliamentary election where—

2.2.1A.b.i

P is or will be registered in a register of parliamentary electors otherwise
than in pursuance of an overseas elector’s declaration or a service
declaration, and

2.2.1A.b.ii

P knows that the person to be appointed is already appointed as proxy to vote
at that election, or at parliamentary elections, for two or more other
electors none of whom is registered in a register of parliamentary electors in
pursuance of an overseas elector’s declaration or a service declaration;

2.2.1A.c

at a local government election in England, where P knows that the person to be
appointed is already appointed as proxy to vote at that election, or at local
government elections in England, for four or more other electors;

2.2.1A.d

at a local government election in England where—

2.2.1A.d.i

P is or will be registered in a register of local government electors in
England otherwise than in pursuance of a service declaration, and

2.2.1A.d.ii

P knows that the person to be appointed is already appointed as proxy to vote
at that election, or at local government elections in England, for two or more
other electors none of whom is registered in a register of local government
electors in England in pursuance of a service declaration;

2.2.1A.e

at parliamentary elections, where P knows that the person to be appointed is
already appointed as proxy to vote at a parliamentary election, or at
parliamentary elections, for four or more other electors;

2.2.1A.f

at parliamentary elections where—

2.2.1A.f.i

P is or will be registered in a register of parliamentary electors otherwise
than in pursuance of an overseas elector’s declaration or a service
declaration, and

2.2.1A.f.ii

P knows that the person to be appointed is already appointed as proxy to vote
at a parliamentary election, or at parliamentary elections, for two or more
other electors none of whom is registered in a register of parliamentary
electors in pursuance of an overseas elector’s declaration or a service
declaration;

2.2.1A.g

at local government elections in England, where P knows that the person to be
appointed is already appointed as proxy to vote at a local government election
in England, or at local government elections in England, for four or more
other electors;

2.2.1A.h

at local government elections in England, where—

2.2.1A.h.i

P is or will be registered in a register of local government electors in
England otherwise than in pursuance of a service declaration, and

2.2.1A.h.ii

at a local government election in England, or at local government elections in
England, for two or more other electors none of whom is registered in a
register of local government electors in England in pursuance of a service
declaration.

2.3.3B.b.i

2.3.3B.b.ii

where the polls for two or more parliamentary elections are held on the same

2.3.3B.c

##### Termination of certain proxy appointments on the specified day

8

8.1

This paragraph applies where—

8.1.a

a proxy appointment is in force immediately before the day specified for the
purposes of this paragraph (“the specified day”) as a result of an application
made before the day on which  paragraph 2 (2)  comes into force, and

8.1.b

the appointment has effect immediately before the specified day in relation
to—

8.1.b.i

parliamentary elections in England and Wales or Scotland or local government
elections in England (or both), or

8.1.b.ii

a particular parliamentary election in England and Wales or Scotland or local
government election in England.

8.2

On the specified day, the proxy appointment ceases to have effect as mentioned
in  sub-paragraph (1) (b) .

8.3

The registration officer must, before the specified day, send the person who
is entitled to vote by proxy by means of the proxy appointment—

8.3.a

a notice informing the person that the appointment ceases to have effect as
mentioned in  sub-paragraph (1) (b)  on the specified day (naming that day),
and

8.3.b

information about how to make a fresh application to vote by proxy.

8.4

As soon as practicable after the specified day, the registration officer must
alter the relevant absent voters’ records as necessary to reflect the change
to the proxy appointment resulting from  sub-paragraph (2) .

8.5

Where the specified day is 31 January in a particular year,  sub-paragraph (6)
applies in relation to a person who—

8.5.a

is entitled (before that day) to vote by proxy by means of the proxy
appointment, and

8.5.b

falls within the category of persons in relation to whom the requirement to
send a regulation 60A notice by that day applies.

8.6

The requirement to send the person a regulation 60A notice by the specified
day does not apply, unless—

8.6.a

the person has an entitlement (or entitlements) due to continue beyond that
day—

8.6.a.i

to vote by proxy at local government elections in Scotland or Wales,

8.6.a.ii

to vote by post (whether as elector or proxy) at parliamentary elections in
England and Wales or Scotland or at local government elections in England (or
both), or

8.6.a.iii

to vote by post (whether as elector or proxy) at local government elections in
Scotland or Wales, and

8.6.b

regulation 60A applies in relation to that entitlement (or those
entitlements).

8.7

Nothing in  sub-paragraph (2)  affects the proxy appointment so far as it also
relates to any election or elections other than those mentioned in  sub-
paragraph (1) (b) .

8.8

In this paragraph—

“ proxy appointment ” means an appointment of a person to vote as proxy for
another person; “ registration officer ” has the meaning given by section 8(1)
of RPA 1983; “ regulation 60A ” means regulation 60A (requirement to provide
fresh signatures) of the Representation of the People (England and Wales)
Regulations 2001 ( S.I. 2001/341 ) or the Representation of the People
(Scotland) Regulations 2001 ( S.I. 2001/497) (S. 2) ;  “ regulation 60A notice
” means a notice under regulation 60A; “ relevant absent voters’ records ”
means the records kept under paragraphs 3(4), 4(6) and 7(6) and (8) of
Schedule 4 to RPA 2000; “ RPA 2000 ” means the Representation of the People
Act 2000; “ specified ” means specified by the Secretary of State in
regulations made by statutory instrument.

9

9.1

This paragraph applies where—

9.1.a

a proxy appointment is in force immediately before the day specified for the
purposes of this paragraph (“the specified day”) as a result of an application
made before the day on which the relevant provisions of this Schedule come
into force, and

9.1.b

the appointment has effect immediately before the specified day in relation
to—

9.1.b.i

parliamentary elections in Northern Ireland, or

9.1.b.ii

a particular parliamentary election in Northern Ireland.

9.2

On the specified day, the proxy appointment ceases to have effect as mentioned
in  sub-paragraph (1) (b) .

9.3

The Chief Electoral Officer for Northern Ireland must, before the specified
day, send the person who is entitled to vote by proxy by means of the proxy
appointment—

9.3.a

a notice informing the person that the appointment ceases to have effect as
mentioned in  sub-paragraph (1) (b)  on the specified day (naming that day),
and

9.3.b

information about how to make a fresh application to vote by proxy.

9.4

As soon as practicable after the specified day, the Chief Electoral Officer
must alter the relevant absent voters’ records as necessary to reflect the
change to the proxy appointment resulting from  sub-paragraph (2) .

9.5

More than one day may be specified for the purposes of this paragraph if the
relevant provisions come into force on different days (and in such a case
references in this paragraph to the specified day and to the relevant
provisions of this Schedule are to be construed accordingly).

9.6

In this paragraph—

“ proxy appointment ” means an appointment of a person to vote as proxy for
another person; “ relevant absent voters’ records ” means the records kept
under sections 6(3) and 9(6) and any lists under sections 7(4) and 9(9) of RPA
1985 which have not been published under regulation 66(3) of the
Representation of the People (Northern Ireland) Regulations 2008 ( S.I.
2008/1741 ); “ relevant provisions of this Schedule ” means paragraphs  2 (2)
and  6 (2) ; “ RPA 1985 ” means the Representation of the People Act 1985; “
specified ” means specified by the Secretary of State in regulations made by
statutory instrument.

##### Termination of applications for certain proxy appointments on the specified day

10

10.1

An application for a proxy appointment that is made before, but not determined
by, the day specified for the purposes of  this paragraph  (“the specified
day”) is to be treated as not having been made so far as the application
relates to—

10.1.a

parliamentary elections in England and Wales or Scotland or local government
elections in England (or both), or

10.1.b

a particular parliamentary election in England and Wales or Scotland or local
government election in England.

10.2

The registration officer must, as soon as practicable, send each person whose
application is affected by  sub-paragraph (1)  information about how to make a
fresh application to vote by proxy.

10.3

Sub-paragraph (1)  does not apply where the application was made on or after
the day on which  paragraph 2 (2)  comes into force.

10.4

Expressions used in  this paragraph  and in  paragraph 8  have the same
meaning as in that paragraph.

11

11.1

An application for a proxy appointment that is made before, but not determined
by, the day specified for the purposes of  this paragraph  (“the specified
day”) is to be treated as not having been made so far as the application
relates to—

11.1.a

parliamentary elections in Northern Ireland, or

11.1.b

a particular parliamentary election in Northern Ireland.

11.2

The Chief Electoral Officer for Northern Ireland must, as soon as practicable,
send each person whose application is affected by  sub-paragraph (1)
information about how to make a fresh application to vote by proxy.

11.3

Sub-paragraph (1)  does not apply where the application was made on or after
the day on which the relevant provisions come into force.

11.4

More than one day may be specified for the purposes of this paragraph if the
relevant provisions of this Schedule come into force on different days (and in
such a case references in this paragraph to the specified day and to the
relevant provisions of this Schedule are to be construed accordingly).

11.5

Expressions used in  this paragraph  and in  paragraph 9  have the same
meaning as in that paragraph.

Undue influence: further provision

is incapable of being elected to or holding—

2.f.i

9.16B.4.c

23

Schedule 9  (electoral misdemeanours) is amended in accordance with paragraphs
24  to  27 .

24

For paragraph 3 substitute—

######### Undue influence

24.3

24.3.1

A person is guilty of undue influence if the person carries out an activity
falling within sub-paragraph  (3)  for the purpose of—

24.3.1.a

inducing or compelling an elector or proxy for an elector to vote in a
particular way or to refrain from voting, or

24.3.1.b

otherwise impeding or preventing the free exercise of the franchise of an
elector or of a proxy for an elector.

24.3.2

A person (“ P ”) is also guilty of undue influence if P carries out an
activity falling within any of paragraphs  (a)  to  (f)  of sub-paragraph  (3)
on account of—

24.3.2.a

an elector or proxy for an elector having voted in a particular way or
refrained from voting, or

24.3.2.b

P assuming an elector or proxy for an elector to have voted in a particular
way or to have refrained from voting.

24.3.3

The following activities fall within this sub-paragraph—

24.3.3.a

using or threatening to use violence against a person;

24.3.3.b

damaging or destroying, or threatening to damage or destroy, a person’s
property;

24.3.3.c

damaging or threatening to damage a person’s reputation;

24.3.3.d

causing or threatening to cause financial loss to a person;

24.3.3.e

causing spiritual injury to, or placing undue spiritual pressure on, a person;

24.3.3.f

doing any other act designed to intimidate a person;

24.3.3.g

doing any act designed to deceive a person in relation to the administration
of an election.

24.3.4

For the purposes of sub-paragraphs  (1)  and  (2)  an activity is carried out
by a person (“ P ”) if it is carried out—

24.3.4.a

by P,

24.3.4.b

by P jointly with one or more other persons, or

24.3.4.c

by one or more other persons on behalf of P and with P’s authority or consent.

25

After paragraph 5 insert—

######### Handling of postal voting documents by political campaigners

25.5ZA

25.5ZA.1

A person who is a political campaigner in respect of a local election is
guilty of a corrupt practice if the person handles a postal voting document
that has been issued to another person for use in that election.

25.5ZA.2

But a person who handles a postal voting document for use in a local election
is not guilty of a corrupt practice if—

25.5ZA.2.a

the person is responsible for, or assists with, the conduct of that election
(for example as a returning officer or a person working under the direction of
a returning officer),

25.5ZA.2.b

the person is engaged in the business of a postal operator, or

25.5ZA.2.c

the person is employed or engaged in a role the duties of which include the
handling of postal packets on behalf of members of an organisation or the
occupants of a communal building,

and the handling is consistent with the person’s duties in that capacity.

25.5ZA.3

Nor is a person guilty of a corrupt practice if the person—

25.5ZA.3.a

is the other person’s spouse, civil partner, parent, grandparent, brother,
sister, child or grandchild, or

25.5ZA.3.b

provides regular care for, or is employed or engaged by an organisation which
provides care for, the other person.

25.5ZA.4

It is a defence for a person charged with the corrupt practice to show that
the person did not dishonestly handle the postal voting document for the
purpose of promoting a particular outcome at a local election.

25.5ZA.5

Where sufficient evidence is adduced to raise an issue with respect to the
defence under sub-paragraph (4), the court must assume that the defence is
satisfied unless the prosecution proves beyond reasonable doubt that it is
not.

25.5ZA.6

For the purposes of this paragraph a person is a political campaigner in
respect of a local election if any of the following paragraphs applies—

25.5ZA.6.a

the person is a candidate at the election;

25.5ZA.6.b

the person is an election agent of a candidate at the election;

25.5ZA.6.c

the person is employed or engaged by a person who is a candidate at the
election for the purposes of that person’s activities as a candidate;

25.5ZA.6.d

the person is a member of a registered political party and carries on an
activity designed to promote a particular outcome at the election;

25.5ZA.6.e

the person is employed or engaged by a registered political party in
connection with the party’s political activities;

25.5ZA.6.f

the person is employed or engaged by a person within any of paragraphs (a) to
(e) to carry on an activity designed to promote a particular outcome at the
election;

25.5ZA.6.g

the person is employed or engaged by a person within paragraph (f) to carry on
an activity designed to promote a particular outcome at the election.

25.5ZA.7

In this paragraph—

“ postal operator ” has the same meaning as in Part 3 of the Postal Services
Act 2011 (see section 27(3) to (5) of that Act); “ postal voting document ”
means a postal ballot paper, declaration of identity or envelope that has been
issued to a person by the returning officer for the purpose of enabling the
person to vote by post at a local election; “ registered political party ”
means a party registered under Part 2 of the Political Parties, Elections and
Referendums Act 2000.

25.5ZA.8

For the purposes of this paragraph, an envelope—

25.5ZA.8.a

that is not a postal voting document, but

25.5ZA.8.b

that contains a postal ballot paper or declaration of identity that has been
issued to a person for the purpose of enabling the person to vote by post at a
local election,

is to be treated as if it were a postal voting document that has been issued
to the person for use in the election.

25.5ZA.9

In this paragraph, any reference to a person who is “engaged” by another
person, or to a person who provides care for another person, includes a
reference to a person who is engaged or provides care otherwise than for
payment or promise of payment.

25.5ZA.10

For the purposes of sub-paragraph (3)(a), two people living together as if
spouses of each other are treated as if they were spouses or civil partners of
each other.

26

26.1

Paragraph 12A (illegal practices: voting offences) is amended as follows.

26.2

After sub-paragraph (1) insert—

26.2.1A

A person (“ P ”) is guilty of an illegal practice if P applies for the
appointment of a proxy to vote for P—

26.2.1A.a

at a local election, where P knows that the person to be appointed is already
appointed as proxy to vote at that election, or at local elections, for four
or more other electors;

26.2.1A.b

at a local election where—

26.2.1A.b.i

P is or will be registered in the register of local electors otherwise than by
virtue of a service qualification, and

26.2.1A.b.ii

P knows that the person to be appointed is already appointed as proxy to vote
at that election, or at local elections, for two or more other electors none
of whom is registered in a register of local electors by virtue of a service
qualification;

26.2.1A.c

at local elections, where P knows that the person to be appointed is already
appointed as proxy to vote at a local election, or at local elections, for
four or more other electors;

26.2.1A.d

at local elections, where—

26.2.1A.d.i

P is or will be registered in the register of local electors otherwise than by
virtue of a service qualification, and

26.2.1A.d.ii

P knows that the person to be appointed is already appointed as proxy to vote
at a local election, or at local elections, for two or more other electors
none of whom is registered in a register of local electors by virtue of a
service qualification.

26.3

For sub-paragraph (4) substitute—

26.3.4

A person is also guilty of an illegal practice if the person votes as proxy—

26.3.4.a

for more than four electors—

26.3.4.a.i

at a local election, or

26.3.4.a.ii

where the polls for two or more local elections are held on the same day, at
those elections taken together;

26.3.4.b

for more than two electors—

26.3.4.b.i

at a local election, or

26.3.4.b.ii

where the polls for two or more local elections are held on the same day, at
those elections taken together,

where the person knows that more than two of those electors are registered in
a register of local electors otherwise than by virtue of a service
qualification.

26.4

In sub-paragraph (6), after “deemed to have voted” insert  “(but see sub-
paragraph (6A))” .

26.5

After sub-paragraph (6) insert—

26.5.6A

For the purpose of determining whether an application for a ballot paper
constitutes an offence under sub-paragraph (2)(a)(i) or (3)(a)(i), a previous
application is to be disregarded if the applicant’s failure to vote on that
occasion resulted only from a failure to produce satisfactory proof of
identity.

27

27.1

Paragraph 27 (requirement of secrecy) is amended as follows.

27.2

In sub-paragraph (3)—

27.2.a

omit “or” at the end of paragraph (d), and

27.2.b

omit paragraph (e).

27.3

After sub-paragraph (3) insert—

27.3.3A

A person is guilty of an electoral offence if the person—

27.3.3A.a

except for some purpose authorised by law, obtains or attempts to obtain
information, or communicates at any time to any other person any information,
as to the number or other unique identifying mark on the back of a ballot
paper sent to a person for voting by post at a local election;

27.3.3A.b

except for some purpose authorised by law, obtains or attempts to obtain
information, or communicates at any time to any other person any information,
as to the official mark on a ballot paper sent to a person for voting by post
at a local election;

27.3.3A.c

obtains or attempts to obtain information, in the circumstances mentioned in
sub-paragraph  (3B) , as to the candidate for whom a person voting by post at
a local election (“ V ”) is about to vote or has voted; or

27.3.3A.d

communicates at any time to any other person information obtained in
contravention of paragraph  (c) .

27.3.3B

The circumstances referred to in sub-paragraph  (3A) (c)  are where V is about
to mark, is in the process of marking, or has just marked, a ballot paper sent
to V for voting by post at the election.

27.3.3C

But—

27.3.3C.a

a person (“ E ”) who is voting by proxy is not guilty of the offence under
sub-paragraph (3A) if E obtains or attempts to obtain from the person
appointed as E’s proxy information as to a matter mentioned in paragraph (a)
or (c) of that sub-paragraph that relates to E’s vote, and

27.3.3C.b

a person who is appointed as proxy for an elector is not guilty of the offence
under sub-paragraph (3A) if the person communicates to that elector
information as to a matter mentioned in paragraph (a) or (c) of that sub-
paragraph that relates to that elector’s vote.

27.3.3D

Sub-paragraph (3A)(c) and (d) does not apply where the purpose (or main
purpose) for which the information is sought or communicated is its use for
the purposes of—

27.3.3D.a

a published statement relating to the way in which voters intend to vote or
have voted at the election, or

27.3.3D.b

a published forecast as to the result of that election which is based on
information given by voters.

27.3.3E

In sub-paragraph  (3D) —

27.3.3E.a

“ forecast ” includes estimate;

27.3.3E.b

“ published ” means made available to the public at large or to any section of
the public, in whatever form and by whatever means;

27.3.3E.c

the reference to the result of the election is a reference to the result of
the election either as a whole or so far as any particular candidate or
candidates at the election is or are concerned.

27.3.3F

A person voting as proxy for an elector at a local election is guilty of an
electoral offence if the person—

27.3.3F.a

communicates at any time to any person other than that elector any information
as to the candidate for whom the person is about to vote, or has voted, as
proxy for that elector; or

27.3.3F.b

except for some purpose authorised by law, communicates at any time to any
person other than that elector any information as to the number or other
unique identifying mark on the back of a ballot paper sent or delivered to the
person for voting as proxy for that elector.

27.4

After sub-paragraph (4) insert—

27.4.5

A person who has undertaken to assist a relevant voter to vote at a local
election is guilty of an electoral offence if the person communicates at any
time to any person except that voter any information as to—

27.4.5.a

the candidate for whom the voter intends to vote or has voted, or

27.4.5.b

the number or other unique identifying mark on the back of the ballot paper
given for the use of the voter.

27.4.6

In sub-paragraph (5) “ relevant voter ” means a voter who is blind, has
another disability, or is unable to read.

###### Transitional provisions relating to proxy voting

32

32.1

This paragraph applies where—

32.1.a

a proxy appointment is in force immediately before the day specified for the
purposes of this paragraph (“the specified day”) as a result of an application
made before the day on which the relevant provisions of this Schedule come
into force, and

32.1.b

the appointment has effect immediately before the specified day in relation to
local elections in Northern Ireland or a particular local election in Northern
Ireland.

32.2

On the specified day, the proxy appointment ceases to have effect as mentioned
in  sub-paragraph (1) (b) .

32.3

The Chief Electoral Officer for Northern Ireland must, before the specified
day, send the person who is entitled to vote by proxy by means of the proxy
appointment—

32.3.a

a notice informing the person that the appointment ceases to have effect as
mentioned in  sub-paragraph (1) (b)  on the specified day (naming that day),
and

32.3.b

information about how to make a fresh application to vote by proxy.

32.4

As soon as practicable after the specified day, the Chief Electoral Officer
must alter the relevant absent voters’ records as necessary to reflect the
change to the proxy appointment resulting from  sub-paragraph (2) .

32.5

More than one day may be specified for the purposes of this paragraph if the
relevant provisions of this Schedule come into force on different days (and in
such a case references in this paragraph to the specified day and to the
relevant provisions of this Schedule are to be construed accordingly).

32.6

In this paragraph and paragraph  33 —

“ the 1985 Order ” means the Local Elections (Northern Ireland) Order 1985 (
S.I. 1985/454 ); “ local election ” has the meaning given by section 130(1) of
the  Electoral Law Act (Northern Ireland) 1962 (c. 14 (N.I.)) ; “ proxy
appointment ” means an appointment of a person to vote as proxy for another
person; “ relevant absent voters’ records ” means— the record kept under
paragraph 1(3) of Part 1 of Schedule 2 to the 1985 Order, the record kept
under paragraph 4(5) of that Part, and any lists kept under paragraphs 2(4)
and 4(8) of that Part which have not been published under paragraph 15(6) of
that Part; “ relevant provisions of this Schedule ” means paragraphs  26  and
28 (2) ; “ specified ” means specified by the Secretary of State in
regulations made by statutory instrument.

##### Transitional provision

###### Interpretation of Part

12

In  this Part —

“ the commencement date ” means the date appointed for section 14 to come
fully into force; “ overseas elector’s declaration ” has the meaning given by
section 2(1) of RPA 1985 (as that provision had effect immediately before the
commencement date); “ RPA 1985 ” means the Representation of the People Act
1985; “ RPA 2000 ” means the Representation of the People Act 2000.

###### Pre-commencement applications for registration in a register of parliamentary electors

13

13.1

The amendments made by section 14 and  Part 1  of  this Schedule  do not apply
in relation to an application for registration in a register of parliamentary
electors in pursuance of a pre-commencement declaration (even if the
application is determined on or after the commencement date).

13.2

In  this paragraph , “ pre-commencement declaration ” means an overseas
elector’s declaration made at any time before the commencement date.

###### Overseas electors registered pursuant to pre-commencement applications

14

14.1

This paragraph  applies to a person who is for the time being registered in a
register of parliamentary electors in pursuance of a pre-commencement
declaration (regardless of when the person’s application for registration in
the register is determined).

14.2

In such a case—

14.2.a

the person is to be treated on and after the commencement date as being
registered in that register in pursuance of a post-commencement declaration on
the basis that the person satisfied the previous registration condition
(within the meaning of  section 1A (2)  of RPA 1985, as substituted by section
14 of this Act);

14.2.b

the address in respect of which the person is registered is the address
specified in the pre-commencement declaration;

14.2.c

sections  1D  and  1E  of RPA 1985 (as substituted by section 14 of this Act)
have effect accordingly, subject to  sub-paragraph (3) .

14.3

Section 1D (1) (a)  has effect as if it provided for the person to remain
registered—

14.3.a

until the end of the period of 12 months beginning with the date when the
person’s entry in the register first takes effect, or

14.3.b

where that period would otherwise end before the specified day, until the end
of that day.

14.4

In  sub-paragraph (3) (b) , “ the specified day ” means the day specified by
the Secretary of State by regulations made by statutory instrument.

14.5

In  this paragraph —

“ pre-commencement declaration ” has the same meaning as in  paragraph 13 ; “
post-commencement declaration ” means an overseas elector’s declaration (as
defined by  section 1B (1)  of RPA 1985 (substituted by section 14 of this
Act)) made at any time on or after the commencement date.

###### Postal voting

15

15.1

This paragraph  applies where, immediately before the commencement date, a
person to whom  paragraph 14  applies has an entitlement to vote by post
(whether as elector or proxy) at parliamentary elections in England and Wales
or Scotland.

15.2

Subject to  sub-paragraph (3) , the person’s entitlement to vote by post ends
on the last day of the period of 12 months beginning with the date when the
person’s entry in the register of parliamentary electors first takes effect
(unless it ends sooner).

15.3

Where—

15.3.a

as a result of  paragraph 14 (3) (b)  the person remains registered in a
register of parliamentary electors until the time referred to in that
provision, and

15.3.b

the person’s entitlement to vote by post would (as a result of  sub-paragraph
(2) ) otherwise end before that time,

the entitlement ends at that time.

15.4

As soon as practicable after the commencement date, the registration officer
must alter the record kept under paragraph 3(4) or 7(6) of Schedule 4 to RPA
2000 (as the case may be) so as to reflect any change resulting from  sub-
paragraph (2)  or  (3)  in the period for which the person’s entitlement to
vote by post lasts.

16

16.1

This paragraph  applies where—

16.1.a

before the commencement date, a person to whom  paragraph 14  applies makes an
application under paragraph 3(1) or 7(4)(a) of Schedule 4 to RPA 2000,

16.1.b

the application is to vote by post (whether as elector or proxy) at
parliamentary elections, and

16.1.c

immediately before the commencement date the application has not been
determined.

16.2

The amendments made to Schedule 4 to RPA 2000 by  Schedule 3  to this Act do
not apply in relation to the determination of the application.

16.3

Any grant of the application is to be for—

16.3.a

the period ending on—

16.3.a.i

the last day of the period of 12 months beginning with the date when the
person’s entry in a register of parliamentary electors first takes effect, or

16.3.a.ii

in a case where  paragraph 14 (3) (b)  applies in relation to the person’s
registration, the time referred to in that provision, or

16.3.b

any shorter period specified in the application.

###### Power to make supplementary provision

17

17.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make provision for supplementing, or
provision incidental to, the provision made by  paragraphs 13  to  16 .

17.2

Regulations under  sub-paragraph (1)  may make different provision for
different purposes or areas.

17.3

Regulations under  sub-paragraph (1)  are to be made by statutory instrument.

17.4

A statutory instrument containing regulations under  sub-paragraph (1)  is
subject to annulment in pursuance of a resolution of either House of
Parliament.

###### Promoting awareness of changes to overseas elector franchise

18

18.1

The Secretary of State may take whatever steps the Secretary of State
considers appropriate to promote awareness among qualifying people of the
changes made by section 14 to the overseas elector franchise.

18.2

In this paragraph—

“ the overseas elector franchise ” means the basis on which a person is
entitled to vote as an elector at parliamentary elections in accordance with
section 1 of RPA 1985; “ qualifying people ” means people who may, on or after
the commencement date, be entitled to vote as electors at parliamentary
elections in accordance with section 1 of RPA 1985.

18.3

A person with functions of a public nature may disclose information to the
Secretary of State for the purpose of enabling the Secretary of State to
identify those who are, or are likely to be, qualifying people.

18.4

The Secretary of State may use information held by, or provided to, the
Secretary of State for the purpose of identifying people who are, or are
likely to be, qualifying people.

18.5

Personal data may not be disclosed or used under this paragraph if the
disclosure or use would contravene the data protection legislation (but in
determining whether the disclosure would do so, the powers conferred by sub-
paragraphs  (3)  and  (4)  are to be taken into account).

18.6

In sub-paragraph  (5) , “ personal data ” and “ the data protection
legislation ” have the same meaning as in the Data Protection Act 2018 (see
section 3 of that Act).

1.11

After section 203 of that Act insert—

########### Meaning of “qualifying EU citizen”

1.11.203A

1.11.203A.1

In this Act “ qualifying EU citizen ” means a person who—

1.11.203A.1.a

is a citizen of a country for the time being listed in  Schedule 6A , and

1.11.203A.1.b

either—

1.11.203A.1.b.i

does not require leave under the Immigration Act 1971 to enter or remain in
the United Kingdom or any of the Islands, or

1.11.203A.1.b.ii

does require such leave but for the time being has (or is, by virtue of any
enactment, to be treated as having) any description of such leave.

1.11.203A.2

The Secretary of State must by regulations add a country to the list in
Schedule 6A  where—

1.11.203A.2.a

the country is a qualifying country,

1.11.203A.2.b

the United Kingdom and the country intend to become parties to a relevant
treaty, and

1.11.203A.2.c

section 20 of the Constitutional Reform and Governance Act 2010 (treaties to
be laid before Parliament before ratification) applies in relation to the
relevant treaty and the requirements of that section have been met such that
the relevant treaty may be ratified.

1.11.203A.3

The Secretary of State may by regulations remove a country from the list in
Schedule 6A  where the country ceases to be a party to a relevant treaty to
which the United Kingdom is also a party.

1.11.203A.4

The Secretary of State must, as soon as reasonably practicable after
regulations are made under subsection  (2)  or  (3) , give notice of that fact
to—

1.11.203A.4.a

registration officers in England,

1.11.203A.4.b

registration officers for elections of police and crime commissioners for
police areas in Wales,

1.11.203A.4.c

the Chief Electoral Officer for Northern Ireland, and

1.11.203A.4.d

the Electoral Commission.

1.11.203A.5

In this section—

“ the Islands ” means the Channel Islands and the Isle of Man; “ qualifying
country ” means a country— that was a member State immediately before IP
completion day, other than the Republic of Ireland, that was part of a member
State immediately before IP completion day, other than the Republic of
Ireland, or that is formed entirely of two or more former countries, both or
all of which were member States immediately before IP completion day, other
than the Republic of Ireland; “ ratification ”, in relation to a treaty, is to
be construed in accordance with section 25(3) of the Constitutional Reform and
Governance Act 2010; “ relevant treaty ” means a treaty containing provision
relating to eligibility to vote and to stand as a candidate at elections; “
treaty ” has the same meaning as in Part 2 of the Constitutional Reform and
Governance Act 2010 (see section 25 of that Act).

########### Meaning of “EU citizen with retained rights”

1.11.203B

1.11.203B.1

In this Act “ EU citizen with retained rights ” means a person who—

1.11.203B.1.a

is a citizen of a country falling within subsection  (8) ,

1.11.203B.1.b

was a citizen of the Union immediately before IP completion day,

1.11.203B.1.c

was resident in the United Kingdom or any of the Islands immediately before
that day,

1.11.203B.1.d

falls within any of subsections  (2)  to (4), and

1.11.203B.1.e

is not a qualifying EU citizen.

1.11.203B.2

A person falls within this subsection if the person—

1.11.203B.2.a

has UK or Islands leave granted by virtue of residence scheme immigration
rules, and

1.11.203B.2.b

has such leave otherwise than in accordance with provision in residence scheme
immigration rules for joining family members.

1.11.203B.3

A person falls within this subsection if—

1.11.203B.3.a

the person has UK or Islands leave but does not fall within subsection (2),
and

1.11.203B.3.b

the requirements of subsection (5) are met in relation to the person.

1.11.203B.4

A person falls within this subsection if—

1.11.203B.4.a

the person does not require UK or Islands leave,

1.11.203B.4.b

the person is resident in the United Kingdom or any of the Islands, and

1.11.203B.4.c

the requirements of subsection (5) are met in relation to the person.

1.11.203B.5

The requirements referred to in subsections (3)(b) and (4)(c) are that—

1.11.203B.5.a

at all times since the relevant date, the person has either had UK or Islands
leave or not required UK or Islands leave, and

1.11.203B.5.b

the person was resident in the United Kingdom or any of the Islands at all
times after the relevant date when the person did not require UK or Islands
leave.

1.11.203B.6

In determining whether the requirement in subsection (5)(a) is met in relation
to a person, any period to which subsection (7) applies is to be disregarded
if the person was resident in the United Kingdom or any of the Islands during
the period.

1.11.203B.7

This subsection applies to any period after the relevant date during which the
person required UK or Islands leave but did not have it, if at the end of the
period the person was granted UK or Islands leave—

1.11.203B.7.a

in pursuance of an application made before the end of the relevant date, or

1.11.203B.7.b

in pursuance of an application made after the relevant date, where the leave
was granted—

1.11.203B.7.b.i

by virtue of residence scheme immigration rules, and

1.11.203B.7.b.ii

otherwise than in accordance with provision in such rules for joining family
members.

1.11.203B.8

A country falls within this subsection where the country—

1.11.203B.8.a

was a member State immediately before IP completion day, other than the
Republic of Ireland,

1.11.203B.8.b

was part of a member State immediately before IP completion day, other than
the Republic of Ireland, or

1.11.203B.8.c

is formed of two or more former countries, at least one of which was a member
State immediately before IP completion day, other than the Republic of
Ireland.

1.11.203B.9

In this section a reference to a person having UK or Islands leave includes a
reference to a person who is, by virtue of any enactment, to be treated as
having such leave.

1.11.203B.10

In this section—

“ the 1971 Act ” means the Immigration Act 1971; “ the Islands ” means the
Channel Islands and the Isle of Man; “ the relevant date ” means 30 June 2021;
“ immigration rules ” has the same meaning as in the 1971 Act; “ residence
scheme immigration rules ” means— residence scheme immigration rules within
the meaning of Part 3 of the European Union (Withdrawal Agreement) Act 2020
(see section 17(1) of that Act), Appendix EU to the Guernsey immigration
rules, Appendix EU to the Isle of Man immigration rules, or Appendix EU(J) to
the Jersey immigration rules; “ UK or Islands leave ” means leave under the
1971 Act to enter or remain in the United Kingdom or any of the Islands.

1.11.203B.11

In this section—

“ Guernsey immigration rules ” means the rules made in respect of the
Bailiwick of Guernsey under sections 1(4) and 3(2) of the 1971 Act as extended
to that Bailiwick; “ Isle of Man immigration rules ” means the rules made in
respect of the Isle of Man under section 3(2) of the 1971 Act as extended to
the Isle of Man; “ Jersey immigration rules ” means the rules contained in the
directions made in respect of the Bailiwick of Jersey under sections 1(4A) and
3(2) of the 1971 Act as extended to that Bailiwick.

1.11.203B.12

References in this section to provision in residence scheme immigration rules
for joining family members are references to—

1.11.203B.12.a

paragraph EU11A or EU14A of Appendix EU to the immigration rules or provision
replacing either of those paragraphs, or

1.11.203B.12.b

provision corresponding to provision within paragraph (a) in the Guernsey
immigration rules, the Isle of Man immigration rules or the Jersey immigration
rules.

1.12

After Schedule 6 to that Act insert—

List of countries for purposes of section  203A

Section  203A

1.12.1

Luxembourg.

1.12.2

Poland.

1.12.3

Portugal.

1.12.4

Spain.

##### Transitional provision etc

###### Holders of elected offices

12

12.1

This paragraph applies where—

12.1.a

immediately before the coming into force of a particular provision of this
Schedule (the “relevant provision”), a person holds an office falling within
sub-paragraph  (4) ,

12.1.b

the person’s term in that office is due to continue after that time, and

12.1.c

apart from this paragraph, the person would become disqualified for continuing
to hold that office as a result of the coming into force of the relevant
provision.

12.2

The coming into force of the relevant provision does not affect the person’s
qualification to continue holding that office until the end of their current
term in that office.

12.3

For the purposes of this paragraph, a person is to be treated as holding an
office from the time when the person is elected as, or declared to be returned
as, the holder of the office (and accordingly the person’s term of office is
to be treated as beginning at that time).

12.4

The following offices fall within this sub-paragraph—

12.4.a

member of the Northern Ireland Assembly;

12.4.b

member of a local authority in England;

12.4.c

elected mayor (within the meaning of Part 1A of the Local Government Act
2000);

12.4.d

mayor for the area of a combined authority established under section 103 of
the Local Democracy, Economic Development and Construction Act 2009;

12.4.da

mayor for the area of a combined county authority established under section  9
(1)  of the Levelling-up and Regeneration Act 2023;

12.4.e

Mayor of London;

12.4.f

member of the London Assembly;

12.4.g

police and crime commissioner.

12.5

In sub-paragraph  (4) (b) , “ local authority in England ” means a county
council in England, a district council, a parish council, a London borough
council or the Council of the Isles of Scilly.

###### Power to make transitional and saving provision

13

13.1

The Secretary of State may by regulations make transitional or saving
provision in connection with provision made by this Schedule.

13.2

Regulations under this paragraph may—

13.2.a

make provision modifying the effect of any statutory provision (including this
Act);

13.2.b

make different provision for different purposes.

13.3

Regulations under this paragraph are to be made by statutory instrument.

13.4

A statutory instrument containing regulations under this paragraph may not be
made unless a draft of the instrument has been laid before and approved by a
resolution of each House of Parliament.

13.5

Nothing in this paragraph affects the generality of section 67 (4)  (power to
make transitional etc provision in connection with commencement).

##### Inchoate offences

53

53.1

An inchoate offence in relation to an offence listed in Part  1  or  2  of
this Schedule.

53.2

In sub-paragraph  (1) , inchoate offence, in relation to an offence, means—

53.2.a

an attempt to commit the offence,

53.2.b

conspiracy to commit the offence,

53.2.c

an offence under Part 2 of the Serious Crime Act 2007 related to the offence,
or

53.2.d

incitement to commit the offence.

53.3

For the purposes of sub-paragraph  (2) (c) , an offence committed by a person
under Part 2 of the Serious Crime Act 2007 (encouraging or assisting crime) is
related to another offence if that other offence is the offence (or one of the
offences) which the person intended or believed would be committed.

##### Armed Forces Act 2006

8

8.1

The Armed Forces Act 2006 is amended as follows.

8.2

After section 236 insert—

########### Disqualification of offenders for holding elective office etc

############ Disqualification orders

8.2.236A

8.2.236A.1

This section applies where—

8.2.236A.1.a

a person (“the offender”) is convicted of a qualifying section 42 offence by a
court,

8.2.236A.1.b

the offender was aged 18 or over when the offence was committed, and

8.2.236A.1.c

the court is satisfied beyond reasonable doubt that the offence is aggravated
by hostility related to persons falling within any of sections 32 to 34 of the
Elections Act 2022.

8.2.236A.2

The court must, when dealing with the offender for the offence, also make an
order (a “disqualification order”) that the offender is disqualified, for the
period of 5 years beginning with the date on which the order is made—

8.2.236A.2.a

for being nominated for election to a relevant elective office, and

8.2.236A.2.b

for being elected to or holding a relevant elective office.

8.2.236A.3

Subsection  (2)  does not apply where the court considers that there are
particular circumstances relating to the offence or to the offender which
would make it unjust in all the circumstances to make the order; and in such a
case the court must state in open court the reasons for not making the order.

8.2.236A.4

For the purposes of this section an offence is aggravated by hostility related
to persons falling within any of sections 32 to 34 of the Elections Act 2022
if—

8.2.236A.4.a

at the time of committing the offence, or immediately before or after doing
so, the offender demonstrated towards the victim of the offence hostility
based on the victim being (or being presumed to be) a person falling within
any of those sections, or

8.2.236A.4.b

the offence was motivated (wholly or partly) by hostility towards persons
falling within any of those sections in their capacity as such.

8.2.236A.5

For the purposes of subsection  (4)  it is immaterial whether or not the
offender's hostility is also based, to any extent, on any other factor not
mentioned in that subsection.

8.2.236A.6

For the purpose of deciding whether to make a disqualification order the court
may consider evidence led by the parties to the proceedings.

8.2.236A.7

It is immaterial whether evidence led in pursuance of subsection  (6)  would
have been admissible in the proceedings in which the offender was convicted.

8.2.236A.8

Where a qualifying section 42 offence is found to have been committed—

8.2.236A.8.a

over a period of 2 or more days, or

8.2.236A.8.b

at some time during a period of 2 or more days,

it is to be taken for the purposes of subsection  (1) (b)  to have been
committed on the last of those days.

8.2.236A.9

For the purposes of any appeal against a disqualification order—

8.2.236A.9.a

references in section 141 to a finding or punishment include the making of a
disqualification order;

8.2.236A.9.b

references in section 16A of the Court Martial Appeals Act 1968 to passing a
sentence include making a disqualification order.

8.2.236A.10

In this section—

                     “ court ” means the court or officer sentencing the
offender;
“ presumed ” means presumed by the offender;
“ qualifying section 42 offence ” means an offence under section 42 (criminal
conduct) as respects which the corresponding offence under the law of England
and Wales is an offence listed in  Schedule 9  to the Elections Act 2022;
“ relevant elective office ” has the same meaning as in Part  5  of the
Elections Act 2022 (see section 37 of that Act).

############ Effect of disqualification order

8.2.236B

References (however expressed) in any enactment to an order under section 30
of the Elections Act 2022 include references to an order under section  236A .
