                 Illegal practices

Section 48

##### Candidates etc at parliamentary, Northern Ireland Assembly and local elections

1

1.1

This paragraph applies if—

1.1.a

apart from this paragraph, a candidate at an election, or an election agent of
such a candidate, would be guilty of an offence under section 48 (1) ,

1.1.b

the election is—

1.1.b.i

a parliamentary election,

1.1.b.ii

an election to the Northern Ireland Assembly,

1.1.b.iii

a local government election within the meaning of section 191 or 203 of RPA
1983,

1.1.b.iv

an election under Part 1A or 2 of the Local Government Act 2000 for the return
of an elected mayor,  ...

1.1.b.v

an election for the return of a mayor for the area of a combined authority,
or

1.1.b.vi

an election for the return of a mayor for the area of a combined county
authority,  and

1.1.c

the offence under section 48 (1)  would relate to the publication of
electronic material which can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve a
purpose within—

1.1.c.i

section 43(4) as it applies to candidates at the election, or

1.1.c.ii

section 45 (5)  as it applies to candidates at the election.

1.2

The candidate or election agent is instead guilty of an illegal practice.

1.3

RPA 1983 applies in relation to the candidate or election agent and the
illegal practice as it applies in relation to a candidate or election agent
and an illegal practice by virtue of section 110(12) (details to appear on
election publications) of that Act.

1.4

In sub-paragraph  (3)  references to RPA 1983 include references to that Act—

1.4.a

as it applies in relation to elections to the Northern Ireland Assembly by
virtue of the Northern Ireland Assembly (Elections) Order 2001 ( S.I.
2001/2599 ),

1.4.b

as it applies in relation to an election under Part 1A or 2 of the Local
Government Act 2000 for the return of an elected mayor by virtue of the Local
Authorities (Mayoral Elections) (England and Wales) Regulations 2007 ( S.I.
2007/1024 ),  ...

1.4.c

as it applies in relation to an election for the return of a mayor for the
area of a combined authority by virtue of the Combined Authorities (Mayoral
Elections) Order 2017 ( S.I. 2017/67 ),  and

1.4.d

as it applies in relation to an election for the return of a mayor for the
area of a combined county authority by virtue of regulations under paragraph
12 (1)  of  Schedule 2  to the Levelling-up and Regeneration Act 2023.

1.5

In this paragraph “ combined authority ” means a combined authority
established under section 103 of the Local Democracy, Economic Development and
Construction Act 2009.

1.6

In this paragraph “ combined county authority ” means a combined county
authority established under section  9 (1)  of the Levelling-up and
Regeneration Act 2023.

##### Candidates etc at elections to the Scottish Parliament

2

2.1

This paragraph applies if—

2.1.a

apart from this paragraph, a candidate at an election to the Scottish
Parliament, or an election agent of such a candidate, would be guilty of an
offence under section 48 (1) , and

2.1.b

the offence under section 48 (1)  would relate to the publication of
electronic material which can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve a
purpose within—

2.1.b.i

section 43(4) as it applies to candidates at the election, or

2.1.b.ii

section 45 (5)  as it applies to candidates at the election.

2.2

The candidate or election agent is instead guilty of an illegal practice.

2.3

The Scottish Parliament (Elections etc.) Order 2015 ( S.S.I. 2015/425 )
applies in relation to the candidate or election agent and the illegal
practice as it applies in relation to a candidate or election agent and an
illegal practice by virtue of article 72(12) of that Order (details to appear
on election publications).

##### Candidates etc at elections to Senedd Cymru

3

3.1

This paragraph applies if—

3.1.a

apart from this paragraph—

3.1.a.i

a constituency or individual candidate at an election to Senedd Cymru or an
election agent of such a candidate, or

3.1.a.ii

a party list candidate at an election to Senedd Cymru or the election agent of
a registered party in relation to that party's list at such an election,

would be guilty of an offence under section 48 (1) , and

3.1.b

the offence under section 48 (1)  would relate to the publication of
electronic material which can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve a
purpose within—

3.1.b.i

section 43(4) as it applies to candidates at the election, or

3.1.b.ii

section 45 (5)  as it applies to candidates at the election.

3.2

The candidate or election agent is instead guilty of an illegal practice.

3.3

The National Assembly for Wales (Representation of the People) Order 2007 (
S.I. 2007/236 ) applies in relation to the candidate or election agent and the
illegal practice as it applies in relation to a candidate or election agent
and an illegal practice by virtue of article 76(12) of that Order (printer’s
name and address on election publications).

3.4

In this paragraph “ constituency candidate ”, “ individual candidate ” and “
party list candidate ” have the same meanings as in that Order (see article
2).

##### Candidates etc at local elections in Scotland

4

4.1

This paragraph applies if—

4.1.a

apart from this paragraph, a candidate at an election, or an election agent of
such a candidate, would be guilty of an offence under section 48 (1) ,

4.1.b

the election is a local government election within the meaning of section 204
of RPA 1983, and

4.1.c

the offence under section 48 (1)  would relate to the publication of
electronic material which can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve a
purpose within—

4.1.c.i

section 43(4) as it applies to candidates at the election, or

4.1.c.ii

section 45 (5)  as it applies to candidates at the election.

4.2

The candidate or election agent is instead guilty of an illegal practice.

4.3

RPA 1983 applies in relation to the candidate or election agent and the
illegal practice as it applies in relation to a candidate or election agent
and an illegal practice by virtue of section 110A(14) of that Act (details to
appear on election publications).

##### Candidates etc at local elections in Northern Ireland

5

5.1

This paragraph applies if—

5.1.a

apart from this paragraph, a candidate at an election, or an election agent of
such a candidate, would be guilty of an offence under section 48 (1) ,

5.1.b

the election is a local election within the meaning of the Electoral Law Act
(Northern Ireland) 1962 (see section 130(1) of that Act), and

5.1.c

the offence under section 48 (1)  would relate to the publication of
electronic material which can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve a
purpose within—

5.1.c.i

section 43(4) as it applies to candidates at the election, or

5.1.c.ii

section 45 (5)  as it applies to candidates at the election.

5.2

The candidate or election agent is instead guilty of an illegal practice.

5.3

The Electoral Law Act (Northern Ireland) 1962 applies in relation to the
candidate or election agent and the illegal practice as it applies in relation
to a candidate or election agent and an illegal practice by virtue of
paragraph 14 of Schedule 9 to that Act (electoral misdemeanours).

##### Candidates at police and crime commissioner elections

6

6.1

This paragraph applies if—

6.1.a

apart from this paragraph, a candidate at an election of a police and crime
commissioner, or an election agent of such a candidate, would be guilty of an
offence under section 48 (1) , and

6.1.b

the offence under section 48 (1)  would relate to the publication of
electronic material which can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve a
purpose within—

6.1.b.i

section 43(4) as it applies to candidates at the election, or

6.1.b.ii

section 45 (5)  as it applies to candidates at the election.

6.2

The candidate or election agent is instead guilty of an illegal practice.

6.3

The Police and Crime Commissioner Elections Order 2012 ( S.I. 2012/1917 )
applies in relation to the candidate or election agent and the illegal
practice as it applies in relation to a candidate or election agent and an
illegal practice by virtue of article 64(12) of that Order (details to appear
on election publications).

##### MPs and recall petitions

7

7.1

This paragraph applies if—

7.1.a

apart from this paragraph, an MP within the meaning of the Recall of MPs Act
2015 would be guilty of an offence under section 48 (1) , and

7.1.b

the offence under section 48 (1)  would relate to the publication of
electronic material which can reasonably be regarded as intended to achieve a
purpose within section 45 (7) .

7.2

The MP is instead guilty of an illegal practice.

7.3

The Recall of MPs Act 2015 (Recall Petition) Regulations 2016 ( S.I. 2016/295
) apply in relation to the MP and the illegal practice as they apply in
relation to an MP and an illegal practice by virtue of regulation 131(9) of
those regulations (details to appear on petition publications).

Supply of information etc

Section 53

##### Supply of information etc

1

1.1

A relevant enforcer may give notice in writing to any person requiring the
person to provide a relevant enforcer, or a person authorised by a relevant
enforcer, with any information which—

1.1.a

is identified in the notice, and

1.1.b

is reasonably required by a relevant enforcer for the purposes of—

1.1.b.i

determining whether electronic material has been published in contravention of
section 41, or

1.1.b.ii

making contact with the promoter of the material or the person on behalf of
whom the material has been published (and who is not the promoter).

1.2

A relevant enforcer may give notice in writing to any person requiring the
person to provide a relevant enforcer, or a person authorised by a relevant
enforcer, with a copy of any electronic material which—

1.2.a

is identified in the notice, and

1.2.b

is reasonably required by a relevant enforcer for the purposes of determining
whether electronic material has been published in contravention of section 41.

1.3

A person to whom a notice is given under this paragraph must comply with it
within such reasonable time as is specified in the notice.

1.4

A relevant enforcer may by notice in writing withdraw or vary a notice under
this paragraph at any time.

##### Court order for disclosure of information etc

2

2.1

This paragraph applies if a relevant enforcer has given a notice under
paragraph  1 (1)  requiring any information to be provided.

2.2

The High Court or (in Scotland) the Court of Session may make an information
disclosure order against a person (“ the respondent ”) if satisfied on an
application by a relevant enforcer that there is information identified in the
notice under paragraph  1 (1)  which—

2.2.a

has not been provided as required by the notice (either within the time
specified in the notice for compliance or subsequently),

2.2.b

is reasonably required by a relevant enforcer for a purpose within paragraph
1 (1) (b) , and

2.2.c

the respondent is able to provide.

2.3

An information disclosure order is an order requiring the respondent to
provide to a relevant enforcer, within such time as is specified in the order,
such information falling within sub-paragraph  (2) (b)  as is identified in
the order.

3

3.1

This paragraph applies if a relevant enforcer has given a notice under
paragraph  1 (2)  requiring any electronic material to be provided.

3.2

The High Court or (in Scotland) the Court of Session may make an electronic
material disclosure order against a person (“ the respondent ”) if satisfied
on an application by a relevant enforcer that there is electronic material
referred to in the notice under paragraph  1 (2)  a copy of which—

3.2.a

has not been provided as required by the notice (either within the time
specified in the notice for compliance or subsequently),

3.2.b

is reasonably required by a relevant enforcer for the purposes of determining
whether electronic material has been published in contravention of section 41,
and

3.2.c

the respondent is able to provide.

3.3

An electronic material disclosure order is an order requiring the respondent
to provide to a relevant enforcer, within such time as is specified in the
order, a copy of such electronic material falling within sub-paragraph  (2)
(b)  as is identified in the order.

##### Power to make copies and records

4

A relevant enforcer, or a person authorised by a relevant enforcer, may make
copies or records of any information or material provided under this Schedule.

##### Authorisation to be in writing

5

An authorisation of a person by a relevant enforcer under this Schedule must
be in writing.

##### Legal professional privilege

6

Nothing in this Schedule requires a person to provide anything in respect of
which a claim to legal professional privilege (or in Scotland to
confidentiality of communications) could be maintained in legal proceedings.

##### Admissibility of information

7

7.1

Information provided by a person (“ P ”) in compliance with a requirement
imposed under this Schedule is admissible in evidence in any proceedings (as
long as it also complies with any requirements governing the admissibility of
evidence in the circumstances in question).

7.2

But in criminal proceedings in which P is charged with an offence other than
one to which sub-paragraph  (3)  applies or in proceedings within sub-
paragraph  (4)  to which both the Commission and P are parties—

7.2.a

no evidence relating to the information is admissible against P, and

7.2.b

no question relating to the information may be asked on behalf of the
prosecution or (as the case may be) the Commission in cross-examination of P,

unless evidence relating to it is adduced, or a question relating to it is
asked, in the proceedings by or on behalf of P.

7.3

This sub-paragraph applies to—

7.3.a

an offence under section 5 of the Perjury Act 1911 (false statements made
otherwise than on oath);

7.3.b

an offence under section 44(2) of the Criminal Law (Consolidation) (Scotland)
Act 1995 (false statements made otherwise than on oath);

7.3.c

an offence under Article 10 of the Perjury (Northern Ireland) Order 1979
(false statements made otherwise than on oath).

7.4

Proceedings are within this sub-paragraph if they arise out of the exercise by
the Commission of any of their powers under Schedule 19C to PPERA.

##### Application of restrictions on disclosure

8

8.1

A disclosure of information pursuant to a requirement under this Schedule does
not breach—

8.1.a

any obligation of confidence owed by the person making the disclosure, or

8.1.b

any other restriction on the disclosure of information (however imposed).

8.2

A duty imposed by virtue of this Schedule does not require a person to
disclose information if to do so would contravene the data protection
legislation (but in determining whether the disclosure would do so, the duty
imposed by virtue of this Schedule is to be taken into account).

8.3

In sub-paragraph  (2)  “ the data protection legislation ” has the same
meaning as in the Data Protection Act 2018 (see section 3(9) of that Act).

##### Meaning of “relevant enforcer”

9

In this Schedule “ relevant enforcer ” means the Electoral Commission or a
constable.
